Woods"}],"pages":{"55290108":{"pageid":55290108,"ns":0,"title":"The Steel Woods","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music group}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = The Steel Woods\n| image            = Main Photo - Shot by @colecreasy.jpg\n| landscape        = yes\n| alt              = \n| caption          = Wes Bayliss, Tyler Powers and Johnny Stanton\n| alias            = \n| origin           = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], United States\n| genre            = {{hlist|[[Country music|Country]]|[[southern rock]]|[[Bluegrass music|bluegrass]]|[[Americana (music)|Americana]]}}\n| years_active     = 2016\u2013present\n| label            = {{hlist|Woods Music|[[Thirty Tigers]]}}\n| associated_acts  = {{flatlist|\n*[[Jamey Johnson]], [[Brent Cobb]]\n}}\n| website          = {{URL|http://thesteelwoods.com}}\n| current_members  = Wes Bayliss<br/>Johnny Stanton<br/>Tyler Powers<br/>\n| past_members     = Jason \"Rowdy\" Cope<br/>Jay Tooke\n}}\n'''The Steel Woods''' are an American [[country music]] group.<ref name=\":0\">{{Citation |date=May 9, 2017 |title=10 New Country Artists You Need to Know: May 2017 |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/country/lists/10-new-country-artists-you-need-to-know-may-2017-w481172/steel-woods-w481175 |access-date=September 19, 2017 }}</ref> from [[Nashville, Tennessee]].<ref>{{Citation |last=Stroud |first=Scott |date=June 1, 2017 |title=Review: The Steel Woods honor southern rock tradition |publisher=[[Associated Press]] |url=http://www.news-sentinel.com/20170601/review-the-steel-woods-honor-southern-rock-tradition&profile=1042M |access-date= September 19, 2017}}</ref> Their debut album, ''Straw in the Wind'', was released in 2017.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.kmuw.org/post/steel-woods-plead-civility-old-news|title=The Steel Woods Plead For Civility With 'Old News'|last=Beaudoin|first=Jedd|website=www.kmuw.org|date=19 June 2019 |language=en|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nThe band has cited influences such as [[Willie Nelson]], [[Waylon Jennings]] and [[Led Zeppelin]],<ref name=\":3\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.wideopencountry.com/artist-to-watch-the-steel-woods/|title=Band to Watch: The Steel Woods, One of Southern Rock's New Revivalists|last=Burchard|first=Jeremy|date=2017-05-17|website=Wide Open Country|language=en-US|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.popmatters.com/the-steel-woods-straw-in-the-wind-2495386212.html|title=The Steel Woods: Straw in the Wind|date=2017-07-19|website=PopMatters|language=en|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref> and have toured [[Opening act|in support]] of artists such as [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]], [[Dwight Yoakam]], [[Jamey Johnson]], [[Cody Jinks]], [[Miranda Lambert]], and [[Blackberry Smoke]].<ref name=\":2\">{{Cite web|url=https://bozone.com/interview-steel-woods-live-divide-eagles-bozeman-june-2019/|title=Interview: Steel Woods @ Live Divide/Eagles Bozeman \u2013 June 2019|date=2019-06-14|website=The BoZone|language=en-US|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nFounding member and guitarist Jason \"Rowdy\" Cope died on January 16, 2021.<ref name=\"Hudak\">{{Cite magazine |last=Hudak |first=Joseph |date=2021-05-20 |title=The Metalhead Who Played Country Guitar |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/jason-rowdy-cope-steel-woods-all-of-your-stones-1172058/ |access-date=2022-09-10 |magazine=Rolling Stone |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n== History ==\nThe Steel Woods were cofounded by Wes Bayliss and Jason \"Rowdy\" Cope. Cope was the creative lead of the band as well as its [[lead guitar]]ist, songwriter and co-producer, while Bayliss is a multi-instrumentalist, lead singer and co-producer.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2019-02-04 |title=Hotstar: The Steel Woods Build A Career Show By Show - Pollstar News |url=https://news.pollstar.com/2019/02/04/hotstar-the-steel-woods-build-a-career-show-by-show/ |access-date=2022-09-12 |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nBayliss grew up in [[Woodland, Alabama]], playing music in his family's gospel band and learned to play harmonica, mandolin, and guitar. In 2007, he moved to [[Mobile, Alabama]], where he experimented further on different instruments. Cope began to learn guitar at the age of 11 in his hometown of [[Asheville, North Carolina]]. He later worked as a [[Los Angeles]]-based musician before moving to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] in 2007 and joined [[Jamey Johnson]]'s band. In his nine years with Johnson, Cope co-wrote \"Can't Cash My Checks\" and helped Johnson make the [[Grammy Award|Grammy]]-nominated \"[[That Lonesome Song]]\" (2008) and \"[[The Guitar Song]]\" (2010).<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.pisgahbrewing.com/shows/the-steel-woods/|title=The Steel Woods|last=Pisgah|first=Brewing|date=July 29, 2019|website=Pisgah Brewing|access-date=April 16, 2020|archive-date=April 8, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170408015228/http://www.pisgahbrewing.com/shows/the-steel-woods/|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn the early days of The Steel Woods, Bayliss and Cope spent a lot of time fishing and writing what would eventually evolve into the bands first studio album, ''Straw in the Wind'' (2017) released on [[Thirty Tigers]]/Woods Music. The album featured a guest vocal appearance by [[Lindi Ortega]], and [[Brent Cobb]] also contributed as a songwriter. On June 10, 2017, it reached number 42 on the [[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] Independent Albums chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/independent-albums/2017-06-09|title=Independent Albums Chart|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nIn the subsequent years, the band toured with fellow [[Southern rock]] artists [[Cody Johnson]], [[Cody Jinks]], [[Whiskey Myers]], and [[Blackberry Smoke]] as well as inspirations such as [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]] and [[Miranda Lambert]].<ref name=\":4\">{{Cite web |title=The Steel Woods \u2013 MoxieTalk with Kirt Jacobs |url=https://moxietalk.com/episodes/thesteelwoods/ |access-date=2020-04-16 |website=MoxieTalk |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nThey recorded their second album, ''Old News'', in [[Asheville, North Carolina|Asheville]] at the site of an old church during a break in their touring schedule. The album was released on January 18, 2019.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://glidemagazine.com/218932/southern-rockers-the-steel-woods-take-a-big-leap-forward-with-riveting-old-news-album-review/ | title=Southern Rockers The Steel Woods Take a Big Leap Forward|website=glidemagazine.com| date=17 January 2019|access-date=2020-04-16}}</ref>\n\nCope died in January 2021.<ref name=\"Hudak\"/> The band's third album, ''All of Your Stones'', was released in May 2021.<ref name=\"ASAOYS\">{{cite web|url=https://americansongwriter.com/review-the-steel-woods-new-album-is-sadly-a-final-testament-to-its-late-co-founder/|title=Review: The Steel Woods' New Album Is Sadly A Final Testament To {{sic|I|t's|nolink=y}} Late Co-Founder|work=[[American Songwriter]]|last=Horowitz|first=Hal|date=May 12, 2021|access-date=May 14, 2021}}</ref>\n\nOn March 28, 2024, Wes Bayliss announced that after the completion of a final United States tour throughout 2024, The Steel Woods would disband, citing personal reasons to end the band and cancelling a scheduled autumn 2024 UK and European tour with fellow Southern rockers [[Blackberry Smoke]].<ref>{{Cite web |title=The Steel Woods Announce They\u2019ll Stop Touring At The End Of 2024 |url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/music/news/the-steel-woods-announce-they-ll-stop-touring-at-the-end-of-2024/ar-BB1kH9nY |access-date=2024-03-29 |website=www.msn.com}}</ref>\n\n==Personnel ==\n* Wes Bayliss \u2013 guitar and vocals\n* Jason Cope \u2013 guitar (d. 2021) \n* Johnny Stanton \u2013 bassist\n* Tyler Powers \u2013 guitar\n* Isaac Senty - drummer\n\n==Discography==\n'''Albums'''\n*''Straw in the Wind'' (2017)\n*''Old News'' (2019)\n*''All of Your Stones'' (2021)<ref name=\"ASAOYS\"/>\n*On Your Time (2023)\n\n==See also==\n* [[List of country music performers]]\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [https://open.spotify.com/artist/69B1gu9EjC0rNb59YYNVPM Spotify]\n* [https://itunes.apple.com/us/artist/the-steel-woods/1073094331?ign-gact=3&ls=1 Apple Music] \n* [https://www.pandora.com/station/play/4477864228065669439 Pandora]\n* [https://play.google.com/music/listen#/wst/artist/A46com75qthwwdnm4wr2arjlvci Google Play Music]\n* {{Discogs artist|The Steel Woods}}\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Steel Woods, The}}\n[[Category:American country rock groups]]\n[[Category:Musical groups established in 2016]]\n[[Category:2016 establishments in Tennessee]]\n[[Category:Musical groups from Nashville, Tennessee]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Montgomery_Gentry","to":"Montgomery Gentry"}],"pages":{"1974368":{"pageid":1974368,"ns":0,"title":"Montgomery Gentry","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=September 2021}}\n{{Short description|American country music duo}}\n{{Good Article}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Montgomery Gentry\n| image             = Montgomery Gentry 2008.jpg\n| image_size        = \n| image_upright     = \n| landscape         = yes\n| caption           = Eddie Montgomery (left) and Troy Gentry at the [[Gretna Heritage Festival]] in 2008\n| origin            = [[Summit, Kentucky]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{hlist|[[Country music|Country]]|[[Southern rock]]|[[country rock]]}}\n| years_active      = 1999\u2013present\n| label             = {{hlist|[[Sony Music Nashville|Columbia Nashville]]|[[Average Joes Entertainment]]|Blaster}}\n| spinoff_of        = Early Tymz\n| website           = {{URL|montgomerygentry.com}}\n| current_members   = {{ubl|Eddie Montgomery}}\n| past_members      = {{ubl|Troy Gentry}}<!--do not add \"Deceased\" as it violates our policies on infoboxes; \"listed in order of joining with no other notation than names.\"-->\n}}\n\n'''Montgomery Gentry''' were an American [[country music]] duo founded by singers Eddie Montgomery and Troy Gentry, both [[Kentucky]] natives. They began performing together in the 1990s as part of two different bands with Montgomery's brother, [[John Michael Montgomery]]. Although Gentry won a talent contest in 1994, he reunited with Eddie Montgomery after Gentry was unable to find a solo record deal, and Montgomery Gentry was formed in 1999. The duo is known for its [[Southern rock]] influences, and has collaborated with [[Charlie Daniels]], [[Toby Keith]], [[Five for Fighting]], and members of [[The Allman Brothers Band]].\n\nMontgomery Gentry released six studio albums for [[Columbia Records]]' Nashville division: ''[[Tattoos & Scars]]'' (1999), ''[[Carrying On]]'' (2001), ''[[My Town (album)|My Town]]'' (2002), ''[[You Do Your Thing]]'' (2004), ''[[Some People Change]]'' (2006), and ''[[Back When I Knew It All]]'' (2008), and a Greatest Hits package. These albums produced more than twenty chart singles on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] chart, including the {{Abbr|No.|Number}} 1 hits, \"[[If You Ever Stop Loving Me]]\", \"[[Something to Be Proud Of]]\", \"[[Lucky Man (Montgomery Gentry song)|Lucky Man]]\", \"[[Back When I Knew It All (song)|Back When I Knew It All]]\", and \"[[Roll with Me]]\". Ten more of their songs reached the Top 10 on the country chart, including the {{Abbr|No.|Number}} 3 hit, \"[[Gone (Montgomery Gentry song)|Gone]]\", the most played country song by a duo in 2005. ''Tattoos & Scars'', ''My Town'', and ''You Do Your Thing'' are all [[music recording sales certification|certified platinum]] by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]]. In 1999, they were awarded Favorite New Artist\u2014Country at the [[American Music Awards]]. Both the [[Academy of Country Music]] and [[Country Music Association]] named them Duo of the Year in 2000, awards for which they were nominated by one or both associations in every year until 2012. In 2009, they were inducted into the [[Grand Ole Opry]].\n\nOn September 8, 2017, Gentry died in [[2017 Medford, New Jersey helicopter crash|a helicopter crash]] in [[Medford, New Jersey|Medford]], New Jersey, where the duo was scheduled to perform that evening. The helicopter pilot died at the scene and Gentry died as he was being rushed to the hospital.<ref name=\"nytmele\">{{Cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/08/arts/music/troy-gentry-dead-country-montgomery-gentry.html?mcubz=0 |title=Troy Gentry of the Country Music Duo Montgomery Gentry Dies at 50 |first=Christopher |last=Mele |newspaper=[[The New York Times]] |date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Despite Gentry's death, Montgomery continues to tour under the Montgomery Gentry name and has pursued a solo career.\n\n==History==\nGerald Edward Montgomery was born September 30, 1963, in [[Danville, Kentucky|Danville]], Kentucky. Troy Lee Gentry (April 5, 1967 \u2013 September 8, 2017) was born in [[Lexington, Kentucky|Lexington]], Kentucky.<ref name=\"whitburn\">{{cite book|last=Whitburn|first=Joel|title=Hot Country Songs 1944 to 2008|publisher=Record Research, Inc|date=2008|page=284|isbn=978-0-89820-177-2}}</ref> When Montgomery was 13 years old, he played drums in his parents' band, Harold Montgomery and the Kentucky River Express.<ref name=\"larkin\">{{cite book|last=Larkin|first=Colin|title=The Encyclopedia of Popular Music|year=2006|publisher=Oxford University Press|page=855}}</ref> In 1990, Montgomery founded the band Early Tymz, which included his younger brother, [[John Michael Montgomery]], and Troy Gentry.<ref name=\"mlive\">{{cite web|url=http://www.mlive.com/entertainment/bay-city/index.ssf/2011/08/montgomery_gentry_heads_to_mid.html|title=Montgomery Gentry has new songs to mix in with many hits|date=August 2, 2011|work=Mlive.com|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\nAfter Early Tymz disbanded, the Montgomery brothers and Gentry briefly performed as Young Country, with John Michael as lead vocalist.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/mydesert/access/1722460821.html?FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Oct+26%2C+2007&author=Judith+Salkin&pub=The+Desert+Sun&desc=Montgomery+Gentry+inherit+outlaw+mantle&pqatl=google|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121108000614/http://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/mydesert/access/1722460821.html?FMT=ABS&FMTS=ABS:FT&type=current&date=Oct+26,+2007&author=Judith+Salkin&pub=The+Desert+Sun&desc=Montgomery+Gentry+inherit+outlaw+mantle&pqatl=google|url-status=dead|archive-date=November 8, 2012|title=Montgomery Gentry inherit outlaw mantle|last=Salkin|first=Judith|date=October 26, 2007|work=The Palm Springs Desert-Sun|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> John Michael left for a solo career in the early 1990s.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> Gentry went solo and won the [[Jim Beam]] National Talent Contest in 1994,<ref name=\"larkin\"/> which led to him opening for [[Patty Loveless]] and [[Tracy Byrd]].<ref name=\"cmt\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/montgomery_gentry/bio.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20040203194048/http://www.cmt.com/artists/az/montgomery_gentry/bio.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=February 3, 2004|title=Montgomery Gentry biography|work=[[Country Music Television|CMT]]|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Gentry initially wanted to pursue a solo career, but after he was unable to find a record deal, he reunited with Eddie Montgomery to form a duo called Deuce, which played at local nightclubs.<ref name=\"cmt\"/> The duo later changed its name to Montgomery Gentry, and signed with [[Columbia Records]]' Nashville division in 1999.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/>\n\n==Musical career==\n===1999\u20132000: ''Tattoos & Scars''===\nMontgomery Gentry released its debut single, \"[[Hillbilly Shoes]]\", in early 1999. It entered the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' country singles charts two weeks before its scheduled release date,<ref name=\"spurs\">{{cite magazine|last=Price|first=Deborah Evans|date=March 6, 1999|title=Strong demand spurs early releases for Columbia's Montgomery Gentry|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|volume=111|issue=10|pages=37, 41|issn=0006-2510|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=8g0EAAAAMBAJ&q=%22montgomery+gentry%22+%221999%22&pg=PA37}}</ref> peaking at number 13 on the country charts and 62 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]].<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> High radio demand for the single led to the label advancing the release date of the duo's debut album, ''[[Tattoos & Scars]]'', from early May to April 6.<ref name=\"spurs\"/>\n\n\"[[Lonely and Gone]]\" was the album's second single, peaking at number 5 on the country charts by year's end. The song was co-written by [[Dave Gibson (American songwriter)|Dave Gibson]] and former [[Pirates of the Mississippi]] lead singer Bill McCorvey. Following it was the top 20 \"[[Daddy Won't Sell the Farm]]\", which won its co-writer, Canadian country singer [[Steve Fox (musician)|Steve Fox]], the 2000 [[Society of Composers, Authors, and Music Publishers of Canada]] (SOCAN) award for Song of the Year.<ref>{{cite book|last=Watson|first=CJ|title=The Everything Songwriting Book: All You Need to Create and Market Hit Songs|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=dR-4SsL7BpgC&q=%22montgomery+gentry%22+%22socan%22+%22song+of+the+year%22&pg=PA256|year=2003|publisher=Everything Books|page=256|isbn=9781440522659}}</ref> After it, Montgomery Gentry charted the number 31 singles \"Self Made Man\" and \"All Night Long\". The latter, which featured guest vocals from [[Charlie Daniels]], was previously the [[b-side]] to \"Hillbilly Shoes\".<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> It was also Daniels' first appearance in the top 40 since \"Mister DJ\" in 1990.<ref>Whitburn, p. 114</ref> The duo won the Vocal Duo of the Year award at the [[Country Music Association]] Awards in late 2000, the first time in eight years that [[Brooks & Dunn]] did not win this award.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> They also won the Top New Vocal Duo or Group award from the [[Academy of Country Music]] and the 2000 Favorite New Artist\u2014Country award at the [[American Music Awards]].<ref name=\"mlive\"/><ref name=\"cmt\"/> By the end of 2000, Montgomery Gentry charted at number 38 with a cover of [[Robert Earl Keen]]'s \"[[Merry Christmas from the Family]]\", itself the b-side to \"All Night Long\".<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> ''Tattoos & Scars'' was [[music recording sales certification|certified platinum]] by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]] (RIAA) in 2001, for shipments of one million copies.<ref name=\"riaa\">{{cite web|url=http://www.riaa.org/goldandplatinumdata.php?resultpage=1&table=SEARCH_RESULTS&artist=montgomery%20gentry&format=album&startYear=1958&endYear=2010&sort=Artist&perPage=25#|title=Search results for Montgomery Gentry|work=[[Recording Industry Association of America]]|access-date=September 13, 2011}}{{Dead link|date=August 2024 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref>\n\nThe album received generally positive reviews for the duo's [[Southern rock]] influences. Thom Jurek of [[Allmusic]] gave it four stars out of five, calling it \"one of the best pop records of the year. Period.\"<ref name=\"tattoos\">{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/tattoos-scars-r402952/review|title=''Tattoos & Scars'' review|last=Jurek|first=Thom|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> and [[Alanna Nash]] of ''[[Entertainment Weekly]]'' rated it \"B\", saying that the album was \"testosterone-laden\".<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.ew.com/ew/article/0,,20034778,00.html|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20081011060149/http://www.ew.com/ew/article/0,,20034778,00.html|url-status=dead|archive-date=October 11, 2008|title=''Tattoos & Scars'' review|last=Nash|first=Alanna|date=April 16, 1999|magazine=Entertainment Weekly|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> In comparison, ''[[Country Standard Time]]'' reviewer Jeffrey B. Remz thought that many of the duo's songs lacked distinctiveness, saying that they seemed to be derivative of Daniels and [[Travis Tritt]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/cdreview.asp?xid=2011|title=''Tattoos & Scars'' review|last=Remz|first=Jeffrey B.|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\n===2001\u20132002: ''Carrying On''===\nMontgomery Gentry's second album, ''[[Carrying On]]'', was released in mid-2001.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web |url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p367958|pure_url=yes}} |title=Montgomery Gentry biography |access-date=September 16, 2011 |last=Huey |first=Steve |publisher=[[AllMusic]]}}</ref> Lead-off single \"[[She Couldn't Change Me]]\" peaked at number 2 on the country charts and number 37 on the Hot 100, making their first Top 40 entry there. The album's only other single, \"Cold One Comin' On\", reached number 23 on the country charts.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> Also included on the album was a cover of [[Waylon Jennings]]' \"[[I'm a Ramblin' Man]]\".<ref name=\"cmt\"/> In March 2002, they charted at number 45 with the track \"Didn't I\", a cut from the soundtrack to the film ''[[We Were Soldiers]]'' which was never officially released as a single.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> The duo promoted the album both on a headline tour sponsored by Jim Beam, and on the Brooks & Dunn Neon Circus & Wild West Tour, which included [[Toby Keith]] and [[Keith Urban]].<ref name=\"cmt\"/><ref name=\"carrying\">{{cite magazine|last=Waddell|first=Ray|date=March 31, 2001|title=Country Duo Montgomery Gentry keeps 'Carrying On'|magazine=Billboard|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|volume=113|issue=13|issn=0006-2510|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=fhQEAAAAMBAJ&q=%22montgomery+gentry%22+%22carrying+on%22&pg=PA29}}</ref> Later in 2002, they toured with [[Kenny Chesney]] on his No Shoes, No Shirt, No Problems tour.<ref name=\"rolling\"/>\n\nMike Kraski, then the senior vice president of sales and marketing at [[Sony Music Nashville]], thought that ''Carrying On'' showed an artistic growth over ''Tattoos & Scars'', and the duo itself thought that ''Carrying On'' was more \"edgy\" in comparison.<ref name=\"carrying\"/> It was less favorably received than its predecessor; William Ruhlmann thought that many of the songs \"sound like they're trying to{{sic}} hard to be macho\",<ref>{{cite web|url=http://allmusic.com/album/carrying-on-r529948/review|title=''Carrying On'' review|last=Ruhlmann|first=William|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> and ''Country Standard Time''{{'}}s Mike Clark thought that the duo was \"playing it safe\", although he described the singles favorably.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/cdreview.asp?xid=2010|title=''Carrying On'' review|last=Clark|first=Mike|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> The album was certified gold for shipments of 500,000 copies.<ref name=\"riaa\"/>\n\n===2002\u20132004: ''My Town''===\nOn August 27, 2002, Montgomery Gentry released ''[[My Town (album)|My Town]]''. After working with producer Joe Scaife on their first two albums, they switched to [[Blake Chancey]]. He allowed them to pick different session musicians than typically used on mainstream country albums, such as [[Chuck Leavell]] and [[Johnny Neel]] of [[The Allman Brothers Band]], whose \"Good Clean Fun\" was covered on it.<ref name=\"my town\">{{cite web|url=http://allmusic.com/album/my-town-r604462/review|title=''My Town''|last=Ruhlmann|first=William|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> They also chose songs co-written by songwriters who had not appeared on their previous albums, including [[Jeffrey Steele]] and [[Rivers Rutherford]].<ref name=\"rolling\">{{cite magazine|last=Waddell|first=Ray|date=August 10, 2002|title=Columbia's Montgomery Gentry is rolling back into 'Town'|magazine=Billboard|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|volume=114|issue=32|page=30|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=BQwEAAAAMBAJ&q=%22montgomery+gentry%22+%22carrying+on%22&pg=PA30}}</ref> The album produced three singles, all co-written by Steele: the [[My Town (Montgomery Gentry song)|title track]] and \"[[Speed (Montgomery Gentry song)|Speed]]\" both at number 5, and \"[[Hell Yeah (Montgomery Gentry song)|Hell Yeah]]\" at number 4.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> Along with [[Blake Shelton]] and [[Andy Griggs]], they contributed a guest appearance on Tracy Byrd's mid-2003 single \"[[The Truth About Men (song)|The Truth About Men]]\", which made the country top 20.<ref>Whitburn, p. 73</ref> In March 2004, ''My Town'' became the duo's second platinum-certified album.<ref name=\"riaa\"/>\n\nRuhlmann gave the album a generally positive review, saying that it \"rocks harder as it goes along\".<ref name=\"my town\"/> On the same site, Rick Cohoon praised \"My Town\" for \"painting in words and music both the pace of living in a small town\",<ref>{{cite web|url=http://allmusic.com/song/my-town-t5722953|title=\"My Town\" review|last=Cohoon|first=Rick|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> and \"Speed\" for being \"slower and more deliberate than the recklessness the title suggests\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://allmusic.com/song/speed-t5722957|title=\"Speed\" review|last=Cohoon|first=Rick|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> On ''Country Standard Time'', Tom Netherland called it \"their third and finest release\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/cdreview.asp?xid=2009|title=''My Town'' review|last=Netherland|first=Tom|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\n===2004\u20132006: ''You Do Your Thing'' and ''Something To Be Proud Of: The Best Of 1999\u20132005''===\n''[[You Do Your Thing]]'', their fourth album, was issued in mid-2004.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> It was led off by \"[[If You Ever Stop Loving Me]]\", which in mid-2004 became Montgomery Gentry's first number 1 single on the country charts. It was also their biggest hit on the Hot 100, reaching number 30 there.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> Following it, the album's title track went to number 22 on the country charts, while \"[[Gone (Montgomery Gentry song)|Gone]]\" peaked at number 3 and \"[[Something to Be Proud Of]]\" became their second number 1 single. The song spent two weeks at number 1, thus making it the first single for Columbia Records' Nashville division to spend more than one week at number 1 since \"[[Daddy's Money]]\" by [[Ricochet (band)|Ricochet]] in 1996.<ref>{{cite magazine|last=Jessen|first=Wade|date=October 15, 2005|title=Between the Bullets: Lambert bows as Sony mates hold lead|magazine=Billboard|page=61|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=5BUEAAAAMBAJ&q=%22next+to+you+next+to+me%22+%22shenandoah%22&pg=PA61}}</ref> \"Gone\" was also the most-played single by a country music duo in 2005,<ref name=\"mlive\"/> and it received a digital gold certification for 500,000 certified [[music download]]s. ''You Do Your Thing'' became their third platinum-selling album.<ref name=\"riaa\"/> Scaife, Chancey, Rutherford, Steele, and [[Mark Wright (record producer)|Mark Wright]] split production duties on the album. Steele also co-wrote \"Gone\" and \"Something to Be Proud Of\" with [[Bob DiPiero]] and Chris Wallin, respectively, while Rutherford and DiPiero co-wrote \"If You Ever Stop Loving Me\" with [[Tom Shapiro]].<ref name=\"liner\">{{cite AV media notes |title=You Do Your Thing |others=Montgomery Gentry |year=2004 |pages=4\u20135 |type=CD booklet |publisher=Columbia Records |id=90558}}</ref> In October 2005, ''You Do Your Thing'' became the duo's third platinum album.<ref name=\"riaa\"/> Rick Bell gave the album a favorable review on ''Country Standard Time'', saying that the duo \"unleash [Southern rock] in a torrent of brash lyrics, wailing guitars, and pounding percussion\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/d/cdreview.asp?xid=2008|title=''You Do Your Thing'' review|last=Bell|first=Rick|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Jurek wrote that it \"is easily the finest outing by modern country's most relevant duo; it rocks, it's soulful, and it's memorable\".<ref name=\"ydyt amg\">{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/r691146/review|title=''You Do Your Thing'' review|last=Jurek|first=Thom|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Montgomery Gentry toured in late 2004 \u2013 early 2005 with [[Trace Adkins]] in support of the album.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1494594/montgomery-gentry-adkins-schedule-2005-tour.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120126130827/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1494594/montgomery-gentry-adkins-schedule-2005-tour.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=January 26, 2012|title=Montgomery Gentry, Adkins Schedule 2005 Tour|date=December 7, 2004|work=CMT|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref>\n\n\"Something to Be Proud Of\" also served as the title track to Montgomery Gentry's first [[greatest hits]] album, ''[[Something to Be Proud Of: The Best of 1999\u20132005]]''. Also included on this disc were \"Didn't I\", \"Merry Christmas from the Family\" and the new song \"[[She Don't Tell Me To]]\" (also co-written by Rutherford, Shapiro, and DiPiero), which peaked at number 5 on the country charts in early 2006.<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> ''Something to Be Proud Of'' was certified gold.<ref name=\"riaa\"/>\n\n===2006\u20132007: ''Some People Change''===\n''[[Some People Change]]'' was the title of Montgomery Gentry's fifth album, which was released in 2006 under the production of Rutherford and Wright. Its [[Some People Change (song)|title track]], co-written by [[Neil Thrasher]], [[Jason Sellers]], and Michael Dulaney,<ref name=\"spc allmusic\"/> was previously recorded by Kenny Chesney on his 2004 album ''[[When the Sun Goes Down (Kenny Chesney album)|When the Sun Goes Down]]''.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/when-the-sun-goes-down-r676324/review|title=''When the Sun Goes Down'' review|last=Erlewine|first=Stephen Thomas|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Gentry told the ''[[Edmonton Sun]]'' that ''Some People Change'' \"is based more on family issues, the love of the family, the love of neighbors, relationships\", and said that the title track \"is about being able to challenge your inner demons and the things that can bring people down, alcoholism, or hatred or racism.\"<ref name=\"edmonton\">{{cite web|url=http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Artists/M/Montgomery_Gentry/2006/08/04/pf-1719269.html|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130115071226/http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Artists/M/Montgomery_Gentry/2006/08/04/pf-1719269.html|url-status=usurped|archive-date=January 15, 2013|title=Montgomery Gentry oppose the fighting|last=Ross|first=Mike|date=August 4, 2006|work=Canoe.ca|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Montgomery Gentry's version of the song peaked at number 7, followed by the two-week number 1 hit \"[[Lucky Man (Montgomery Gentry song)|Lucky Man]]\" and the number 3 \"[[What Do Ya Think About That]]\".<ref name=\"whitburn\"/> In 2008, \"Lucky Man\" was nominated for the [[Grammy Award for Best Country Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal]], the duo's first Grammy nomination.<ref name=\"vaught\">{{cite web|url=http://articles.centralkynews.com/2007-12-06/news/24863732_1_montgomery-gentry-eddie-montgomery-troy-gentry|title=Breaking News: Montgomery Gentry nominated for Grammy Award|last=Vaught|first=Larry|date=December 6, 2007|work=Central Kentucky News|access-date=September 16, 2011|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120402130645/http://articles.centralkynews.com/2007-12-06/news/24863732_1_montgomery-gentry-eddie-montgomery-troy-gentry|archive-date=April 2, 2012}}</ref>\n\n''Some People Change'' was Montgomery Gentry's lowest-selling album at the time. Joe Galante, then-president of Sony Music Nashville, thought that the album's poor sales were because it \"strayed musically from what the base had been. They have an edge to their sound, and I think we got a little too soft.\"<ref name=\"yahoo\">{{cite news |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/music-gentry-dc/montgomery-gentry-gets-back-in-focus-on-new-album-idUKN1644075120080516 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170910041203/http://uk.reuters.com/article/music-gentry-dc/montgomery-gentry-gets-back-in-focus-on-new-album-idUKN1644075120080516 |url-status=dead |archive-date=September 10, 2017 |title=Montgomery Gentry gets 'Back' in focus on new album |first=Ken |last=Tucker |access-date=September 9, 2017 |date=May 18, 2008 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref> Kelefa Sanneh of ''[[The New York Times]]'' gave a mixed review, saying that it was more \"touchy-feely\" than ''You Do Your Thing'', and that \"no one works a snarling country chorus like Montgomery Gentry\".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://select.nytimes.com/gst/abstract.html?res=F20F1FFC3C5B0C708EDDA90994DE404482|title=Critics' Choice: New CD's|last=Sanneh|first=Kelefa|date=October 23, 2006|work=The New York Times|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Chris Willman of ''Entertainment Weekly'' gave the album a \"C\", criticizing the duo for the contradictory viewpoints of personal changes on the title track versus the \"defense of the American right to piss off your neighbors\" in \"What Do Ya Think About That\".<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.ew.com/ew/article/0,,1548446,00.html|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090425203918/http://www.ew.com/ew/article/0,,1548446,00.html|url-status=dead|archive-date=April 25, 2009|title=''Some People Change'' review|last=Willman|first=Chris|date=October 20, 2006|magazine=Entertainment Weekly|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Jurek comparatively called it a \"masterpiece\" and said that it was \"a new pinnacle for the duo\", calling the title track \"one of those tunes that defines something that lies at the heart of what is good about Americans.\"<ref name=\"spc allmusic\">{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/some-people-change-r860437/review|title=''Some People Change'' review|last=Jurek|first=Thom|work=Allmusic|access-date=October 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\n===2008\u20132009: ''Back When I Knew It All''===\nIn 2008, the duo went to the Ardent studios in [[Memphis, Tennessee|Memphis]], Tennessee, to record their sixth album, ''[[Back When I Knew It All]]''. Once again, they worked with Blake Chancey as producer.<ref name=\"yahoo\"/> This album's [[Back When I Knew It All (song)|title track]], co-written by [[Trent Willmon]], was the duo's fastest-climbing single.<ref name=\"yahoo\"/> Both it and followup \"[[Roll with Me]]\", which included a backing vocal from [[Five for Fighting]],<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=1548|title=Montgomery Gentry release new disc June 10|date=March 31, 2008|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> went to number 1. \"[[One in Every Crowd]]\", co-written by Montgomery with Kim Tribble and former [[Trick Pony]] bassist Ira Dean, was issued in January 2009 as the third single. By the middle of the year, this song peaked at number 5. The fourth single, the number 23 \"[[Long Line of Losers]]\", was co-written and previously recorded by [[Kevin Fowler]]. [[Toby Keith]], with whom Montgomery Gentry toured in mid-2008, contributed a guest vocal on the [[Terri Clark]] co-write \"I Pick My Parties\",<ref name=\"yahoo\"/><ref name=\"allmusic back\"/> and Lillie Mae Rische of [[Jypsi]] made an appearance on \"God Knows Who I Am\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_headlines/article/0,3034,GAC_26063_5854357_,00.html|title=Montgomery Gentry Looks to Get \"Raucous\"|date=April 24, 2008|work=Great American Country|access-date=October 13, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120401033328/http://www.gactv.com/gac/nw_headlines/article/0,3034,GAC_26063_5854357_,00.html|archive-date=April 1, 2012|url-status=dead}}</ref> Thom Jurek wrote of this album, \"The hardcore fans will love it, but this isn't the album that will win over many new ones.\"<ref name=\"allmusic back\">{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/back-when-i-knew-it-all-r1385272/review|title=''Back When I Knew It All'' review|last=Jurek|first=Thom|work=Allmusic|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref>\n\nOn May 26, 2009, Montgomery Gentry was formally invited by [[Charlie Daniels]] to become members of the [[Grand Ole Opry]]. [[Marty Stuart]] and [[Little Jimmy Dickens]] inducted them on June 23.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://new.music.yahoo.com/montgomery-gentry/news/montgomery-gentry-inducted-into-grand-ole-opry--61990467|title=Montgomery Gentry inducted into Grand Ole Opry|date=June 24, 2009|agency=Associated Press|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> Also in May 2009, [[Cracker Barrel]] restaurants released an exclusive compilation titled ''For Our Heroes'', which included some of their hits along with \"Didn't I\" and three other songs which had previously been released only as bonus tracks. The restaurant chain donated a portion of all profits from the album to the [[Wounded Warrior Project]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1613121/cmt-insider-montgomery-gentry-cd-assists-wounded-warrior-project.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090606224941/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1613121/cmt-insider-montgomery-gentry-cd-assists-wounded-warrior-project.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=June 6, 2009|title=CMT Insider: Montgomery Gentry CD Assists Wounded Warrior Project|date=June 2, 2009|work=CMT|access-date=October 13, 2011}}</ref>\n\n===2009\u20132011: ''Freedom'' and ''Hits And More: Life Beside A Gravel Road''===\nOn November 30, 2009, Montgomery Gentry released the single \"Oughta Be More Songs About That\". It was to have been included on an album titled ''Freedom'', which was to have included a song that the two wrote with Gary Hannan and Phil O'Donnell titled \"Freedom Never Goes Out of Style\".<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/960713/montgomery-gentry-freedom-album-preview|title=Montgomery Gentry \"Freedom\" Album Preview|last=Graff|first=Gary|date=January 12, 2010|magazine=Billboard|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> The label scrapped ''Freedom'' and instead chose to release an [[extended play]] titled ''Hits and More: Life Beside a Gravel Road'',<ref name=\"boot\">{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2010/09/17/montgomery-gentry-columbia-records/|title=Montgomery Gentry Leave Columbia Records|last=Horner|first=Marianne|date=September 17, 2010|work=The Boot|access-date=September 17, 2010}}</ref> which would have included past hits and three new songs. Its first single, \"While You're Still Young\",<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1637352/montgomery-gentry-ship-new-single-while-youre-still-young.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100524150159/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1637352/montgomery-gentry-ship-new-single-while-youre-still-young.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=May 24, 2010|title=Montgomery Gentry Ship New Single, \"While You're Still Young\"|date=April 19, 2010|work=CMT|access-date=June 19, 2010}}</ref> peaked at number 32 in mid-2010. On September 17, 2010, a day before the extended play's slated release, Montgomery Gentry exited the label,<ref name=\"boot\"/> and ''Hits and More'' was shelved.<ref name=\"butt\"/> Both members told ''[[Country Weekly]]'' that they decided to leave Columbia because \"there were so many people trying to encourage us to do something a little different musically. Some of it worked and some of it didn't.\"<ref name=\"butt\"/>\n\n===2011\u20132012: ''Rebels On The Run'' and ''Friends and Family''===\nMontgomery Gentry signed to [[Average Joes Entertainment]], a label co-owned by [[country rap]] artist [[Colt Ford]], in March 2011.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1659236/montgomery-gentry-sign-to-average-joes-entertainment.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110308041508/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1659236/montgomery-gentry-sign-to-average-joes-entertainment.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=March 8, 2011|title=Montgomery Gentry sign to Average Joe's Entertainment|date=March 4, 2011|work=CMT|access-date=March 4, 2011}}</ref> Their first release for the label, \"[[Where I Come From (Montgomery Gentry song)|Where I Come From]]\", appears on their seventh album ''[[Rebels on the Run]]'',<ref name=\"rebels\">{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2011/08/18/montgomery-gentry-rebels-on-the-run-new-album/|title=Montgomery Gentry Are 'Rebels on the Run'|last=Thompson|first=Gayle|date=August 18, 2011|work=The Boot|access-date=September 13, 2011}}</ref> released on October 18.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/r2273647|title=''Rebels on the Run''|work=Allmusic|access-date=October 13, 2011}}</ref> The album was produced by [[Michael Knox (record producer)|Michael Knox]], who also produces for [[Jason Aldean]].<ref>{{cite news|last=Conaway|first=Alanna|title=Montgomery Gentry to Release New 'Rebels on the Run' Album on October 4|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/montgomery-gentry-rebels-on-the-run-october-4/|access-date=September 21, 2011|newspaper=Taste of Country|date=August 19, 2011}}</ref> Jurek thought that the album was \"the most consistent offering\" since ''Some People Change'' \"even if it doesn't quite scale those heights\",<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/rebels-on-the-run-r2273647/review|title=''Rebels on the Run'' review|last=Jurek|first=Thom|work=Allmusic|access-date=October 21, 2011}}</ref> and ''Country Weekly'' reviewer Jessica Nicholson called it \"classic Montgomery Gentry\".<ref name=\"weekly\">{{cite journal|last=Nicholson|first=Jessica|date=October 31, 2011|title=Reviews|journal=[[Country Weekly]]|volume=18|issue=45|page=56|issn=1074-3235}}</ref> In early 2012, \"Where I Come From\" peaked at number 8 on the country charts. It was followed by \"So Called Life\", which failed to make Top 40.\n\nOn October 23, 2012, the duo released a digital-only EP titled ''Friends and Family.'' The EP contains four tracks, including \"I'll Keep the Kids\", which was released as a single.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://blog.gactv.com/blog/2012/10/24/montgomery-gentry-releases-friends-and-family-ep/|title=Montgomery Gentry Releases Friends and Family EP|last=Wyland|first=Sarah|date=October 24, 2012|work=Great American Country|access-date=July 28, 2013|archive-date=September 17, 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130917031420/http://blog.gactv.com/blog/2012/10/24/montgomery-gentry-releases-friends-and-family-ep/|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n===2013\u20132015: ''Folks Like Us''===\nThe duo spent the better part of 2012 and 2013 touring. They signed to Blaster Records in February 2014 and announced that a new album, to be produced by [[Michael Knox (record producer)|Michael Knox]], would be released within the year.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.montgomerygentry.com/329-blaster-records-signs-montgomery-gentry |access-date=January 6, 2015 }}</ref> However, the album's lead single, titled \"Headlights\", did not perform as expected on the charts, peaking at number 44 on Country Airplay. As a result, the album's release was delayed.<ref>{{cite magazine |title=Montgomery Gentry Tease Early 2015 Release for New Album|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/6274176/montgomery-gentry-early-2015-release-new-album|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |date=October 6, 2014|access-date=September 21, 2015}}</ref> The album's second single \"Folks Like Us\", was released to country radio in March 2015. ''[[Folks Like Us]]'' was released on June 9, 2015.<ref name=folkslikeus>{{cite news|last1=Thompson|first1=Gayle|title=Montgomery Gentry Announce New Album, 'Folks Like Us'|url=http://theboot.com/montgomery-gentry-folks-like-us-album/|access-date=April 11, 2015|work=The Boot|date=April 8, 2015}}</ref>\n\n===2016\u2013present: Gentry's death, ''Here's to You'', ''20 Years of Hits'', ''Outskirts'' and Montgomery's first solo studio album===\nIn November 2016, the duo left Blaster Records and re-signed with [[Average Joes Entertainment]]. They began working on a new album, then slated for a 2017 release.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://averagejoesent.com/montgomery-gentry-returns-average-joes/ |title=Montgomery Gentry Returns to Average Joes |website=[[Average Joes Entertainment]] |access-date=September 8, 2017}}</ref> Following Gentry's death on September 8, 2017, the label announced that the duo had completed their new album prior to the fatal helicopter crash.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/montgomery-gentry-new-album-2017/|title=Montgomery Gentry Recently Completed a New Album, Label Says|website=The Boot|date=September 9, 2017 |access-date=February 3, 2018}}</ref> \"Better Me\", the lead single, was released on September 15, 2017.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/montgomery-gentry-song-better-me/|title=New Montgomery Gentry Song 'Better Me' Is a 'Perfect Epitaph' for Troy Gentry|work=Taste of Country|date=September 13, 2017|last=Dukes|first=Billy}}</ref> In November 2017, the album's title ''[[Here's to You (Montgomery Gentry album)|Here's to You]]'' was announced, as was its release date of February 2, 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/montgomery-gentry-heres-to-you-final-album/|title=Montgomery Gentry's Final Album Coming in February|last=Stefano|first=Angela|date=November 8, 2017|work=The Boot|access-date=November 13, 2017}}</ref> Montgomery has confirmed that he will continue the Montgomery Gentry name as a solo act due to Gentry's death and he plans to tour in 2018 in support of the new album.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/2018/01/19/eddie-montgomery-decision-continue-montgomery-gentry/1049754001/|title=Eddie Montgomery: The decision to continue Montgomery Gentry|website=Tennessean.com|access-date=February 3, 2018}}</ref>  On November 16, Average Joes issued the new compilation ''20 Years of Hits'', which includes new re-recordings of the duo's biggest hits that were completed before Gentry's death.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://montgomerygentry.com/news/457094/montgomery-gentry-20-years-of-hits-set-for-release |title=\"MONTGOMERY GENTRY: 20 YEARS OF HITS\" SET FOR RELEASE NOVEMBER 16, 2018 - Montgomery Gentry |access-date=November 27, 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181127110223/https://montgomerygentry.com/news/457094/montgomery-gentry-20-years-of-hits-set-for-release |archive-date=November 27, 2018 |url-status=dead }}</ref> This was followed in 2019 by the studio album ''Outskirts'', a seven-song compilation recorded a week prior to Gentry's death. Produced by [[Noah Gordon (singer)|Noah Gordon]] and Shannon Houchins, the album includes a cover of [[Merle Haggard]]'s 1983 hit \"[[What Am I Gonna Do (With the Rest of My Life)]]\" and [[Darrell Scott]]'s \"You'll Never Leave Harlan Alive\".<ref>{{Cite web |url=http://www.nashcountrydaily.com/2019/05/16/montgomery-gentry-to-release-new-7-song-ep-outskirts/ |title=Montgomery Gentry to Release New 7-Song EP, \"Outskirts\" &#124; Nash Country Daily |access-date=December 15, 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191215173107/http://www.nashcountrydaily.com/2019/05/16/montgomery-gentry-to-release-new-7-song-ep-outskirts/ |archive-date=December 15, 2019 |url-status=dead }}</ref> Later in the year, the label released a deluxe version with additional songs. At the time of the album's release, Montgomery said that he planned to continue touring under the Montgomery Gentry name even after Gentry's death, and that he wanted to honor Gentry by releasing songs that they had worked on prior.<ref>{{cite web|last=Thompson |first=Gayle |url=https://popculture.com/country-music/2019/10/30/montgomery-gentry-releases-last-live-performance-footage-outskirts/ |title=Montgomery Gentry Releases Last Live Performance Footage of 'Outskirts' (Exclusive) |website=Popculture.com |date=November 1, 2019 |access-date=April 5, 2020}}</ref>\n\nOn October 29, 2021, Montgomery released his first studio album as a solo artist titled ''Ain't No Closing Me Down'' via [[Average Joes Entertainment]] label. The album features two singles \"Alive And Well\" and \"My Son\".<ref>{{cite web | url=https://people.com/country/eddie-montgomery-releases-my-son-talks-pain/ | title=Eddie Montgomery Opens Up About the Pain He's Been Carrying Around for a 'Long Time' | publisher=People | date=October 1, 2021 | accessdate=July 6, 2022}}</ref> While maintaining his solo career, Montgomery has also continued to tour with the backing band under the Montgomery Gentry name.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://tasteofcountry.com/eddie-montgomery-alive-and-well/ | title=Eddie Montgomery Shares His First Single as a Solo Artist, 'Alive and Well' | publisher=[[Taste of Country]] | date=August 30, 2021 | accessdate=August 12, 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Musical styles==\nMontgomery Gentry's sound was defined by [[Southern rock]] influences. Steve Huey of Allmusic wrote that the duo \"evokes the sound and spirit of Southern rockers like [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]], the [[Marshall Tucker Band]], and Charlie Daniels, painting themselves as rowdy redneck rebels who still hold small-town values.\"<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> They cite Daniels, Lynyrd Skynyrd and [[Hank Williams, Jr.]] as primary musical influences.<ref name=\"cmtgray\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1443581/montgomery-gentry-carrying-on-with-macho-country.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160213110824/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1443581/montgomery-gentry-carrying-on-with-macho-country.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=February 13, 2016|title=Montgomery Gentry 'Carrying On' With Macho Country|last=Gray|first=Michael|date=May 4, 2001|work=CMT|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref> Montgomery and Gentry alternated as lead vocalists, with Gentry often accompanying on [[acoustic guitar]].<ref name=\"mlive\"/> Jurek wrote that \"Montgomery's rough hewn baritone and Gentry's almost unreal range and trademark phrasing make something highly original\".<ref name=\"tattoos\"/> In his book ''Country'', Richard Carlin describes Montgomery Gentry as \"rock[ing] harder than [[Brooks & Dunn]], although their music could be seen as an extension of that successful pair's boot-scootin' sound.\" He also wrote that Gentry sings with a \"sweet, high tenor\" while Montgomery \"complements with an earthy, sometimes raspy, baritone\", and notes that the duo has an \"energetic stage show and dress\".<ref>{{cite book|last=Carlin|first=Richard|title=Country|year=2006|publisher=Infobase Publishing|page=142}}</ref>\n\nMany of the duo's mid-tempo songs, such as \"My Town\", centralized on a theme of rural lifestyles.<ref name=\"my town\"/> Others, such as \"You Do Your Thing\"<ref name=\"ydyt amg\"/> and \"Some People Change\", contained messages of tolerance towards others with differing opinions.<ref name=\"edmonton\"/>\n\n==Personal lives==\n===Eddie Montgomery===\nGerald Edward \"Eddie\" Montgomery was born in [[Danville, Kentucky|Danville]], Kentucky, on September 30, 1963, to parents Carol Dean (n\u00e9e Lay) and Harold Edward Montgomery (1941\u20131994).\n\nIn November 2010, Eddie Montgomery told [[Great American Country]] that he had been diagnosed with [[prostate cancer]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://blog.gactv.com/blog/2010/11/18/eddie-montgomery-diagnosed-with-cancer/|title=Eddie Montgomery Diagnosed With Cancer|last=Newcomer|first=Wendy|date=November 18, 2010|work=Great American Country|access-date=November 19, 2010|archive-date=July 25, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110725045544/http://blog.gactv.com/blog/2010/11/18/eddie-montgomery-diagnosed-with-cancer/|url-status=dead}}</ref> The cancer was successfully removed a month later.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2010/12/18/eddie-montgomery-surgery-cancer/|title=Eddie Montgomery Beats Prostate Cancer|last=Duvall|first=Erin|date=December 18, 2010|work=The Boot|access-date=March 4, 2011}}</ref> The same month, his wife, Tracy Nunan Montgomery,<ref name=\"People Magazine\">{{cite web|last1=Anderson|first1=Danielle|title=Hunter Montgomery's Devastated Mom Reveals He Died from an Overdose: We Hope His Story Helps Others|url=http://people.com/country/hunter-montgomery-dead-of-drug-overdose-mom-hopes-story-helps-others/|website=People.com|publisher=People Magazine|access-date=September 9, 2017}}</ref> announced their divorce,<ref name=\"rebels\"/> serving him papers at Eddie Montgomery's Steakhouse, a restaurant he owned in [[Harrodsburg, Kentucky|Harrodsburg]], Kentucky. The restaurant closed abruptly in Spring 2013. The couple had four children and had been married for over 20 years.<ref name=\"butt\">{{cite journal|last=Paxman|first=Bob|date=October 10, 2011|title=Back & kickin' butt: Montgomery Gentry whips out a new collection of hard-driving, honky-tonk anthems\u2014just like in the old days|journal=[[Country Weekly]]|volume=18|issue=41|pages=42\u201346|issn=1074-3235}}</ref> Montgomery posted to Twitter and Facebook that she divorced him because she did not want to \"cope with his illness,\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=4799|title=Eddie Montgomery's wife sues for divorce|date=December 1, 2010|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref> but she subsequently denied it.<ref name=\"Country Music Television\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1653406/eddie-montgomerys-wife-says-his-cancer-did-not-affect-divorce-decision.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101205050313/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1653406/eddie-montgomerys-wife-says-his-cancer-did-not-affect-divorce-decision.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=December 5, 2010|title=Eddie Montgomery's Wife Says His Cancer Did Not Affect Divorce Decision|date=December 2, 2010|work=CMT|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref> Montgomery subsequently married his longtime girlfriend, Jennifer Belcher, in 2014.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/eddie-montgomery-married/|title=Eddie Montgomery Gets Married|website=The Boot|date=April 29, 2014 |language=en-US|access-date=September 11, 2017}}</ref> On September 27, 2015, Montgomery wrote that his and ex-wife Tracy Nunan's 19-year-old son, Hunter, had been killed in an accident.<ref name=\"cnn\">{{cite news|url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/09/27/entertainment/eddie-montgomery-son-dies-feat/index.html|title=Country Star Eddie Montgomery's Son Dies|last=Hunter|first=Marnie|date=September 27, 2015|access-date=September 27, 2015|work=CNN}}</ref> Nunan subsequently clarified that Hunter died of an overdose, which she believed was accidental.<ref name=\"People Magazine\"/>\n\n===Troy Gentry===\nTroy Gentry was born on April 5, 1967, in Lexington, Kentucky, to Patricia and Lloyd Gentry. He had a brother, Keith Gentry, and a sister, Jana Gentry Eckhardt. He graduated from Lexington Community College and attended the University of Kentucky.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/troy-gentry-obituary/|title=Read Troy Gentry's Official Obituary|website=The Boot|date=September 11, 2017 |language=en-US|access-date=September 12, 2017}}</ref> Gentry married Angie McClure in 1999.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=QadeAAAAIBAJ&pg=2695,2389280&dq=troy-gentry+angie&hl=en|title=Gary Allan will play Eddie Cochran in upcoming mini-series|last=Chatfield|first=K.C.|date=August 22, 1999|work=Portsmouth Daily Times|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref> They had a child, Kaylee, who was born in November 2002.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1458700/its-a-girl-for-troy-gentry-wife.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120126130832/http://www.cmt.com/news/news-in-brief/1458700/its-a-girl-for-troy-gentry-wife.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=January 26, 2012|title=It's a Girl for Troy Gentry, Wife|date=November 14, 2002|work=CMT|access-date=September 16, 2011}}</ref> He also had a child, Taylor, from a previous marriage.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/troy-gentry-montgomery-gentry-dies-helicopter-crash/story?id=49711197|title=Troy Gentry of Montgomery Gentry dies in helicopter crash|last=Dresdale|first=Andrea|date=September 8, 2017|publisher=ABC News|access-date=September 12, 2017}}</ref>\n\nIn 2004, Gentry purchased a [[American black bear|black bear]] named \"Cubby\" from a facility called the Minnesota Wildlife Connection and subsequently shot the bear from inside an electrified enclosure, a practice commonly known as [[Canned hunt|canned hunting]]. On November 27, 2006, Gentry pleaded guilty to a charge of falsely tagging a bear that was killed in a fenced enclosure as if it had been killed in the wild.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://new.music.yahoo.com/montgomery-gentry/news/troy-gentry-pleads-guilty-to-bear-charge--35244681 |title=Troy Gentry pleads guilty to bear charge |date=November 27, 2006 |agency=Associated Press |access-date=September 13, 2011 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110813003533/http://new.music.yahoo.com/montgomery-gentry/news/troy-gentry-pleads-guilty-to-bear-charge--35244681 |archive-date=August 13, 2011 }}</ref> Under the plea agreement, he agreed to pay a $15,000 fine; give up hunting, fishing, and trapping in Minnesota for five years; and forfeit Cubby's taxidermied remains and the bow he used to shoot Cubby.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://usatoday30.usatoday.com/life/people/2006-11-28-gentry-sorry_x.htm|title=Gentry issues mea culpa for 'Cubby' the bear killing|date=November 28, 2006|publisher=USA Today|access-date=September 12, 2017}}</ref> In a statement that he posted on the duo's website on November 9, 2010, he apologized for his actions as well as the unethical manner in which he killed Cubby.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://wycd.cbslocal.com/2010/11/22/troy-gentry-bear-hunting-incident/|title=Troy Gentry Apologizes Again!|date=November 22, 2010|publisher=WYCD|access-date=September 12, 2017}}</ref>\n\nOn September 8, 2017, Gentry [[2017 Medford, New Jersey helicopter crash|died in a helicopter crash]] while taking a helicopter tour of [[Medford, New Jersey|Medford]], New Jersey, where he and Montgomery were set to perform that evening.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.lex18.com/story/36322963/troy-gentry-of-montgomery-gentry-killed-in-helicopter-crash|title=Troy Gentry Of Montgomery Gentry Killed In Helicopter Crash|date=September 8, 2017|work=LEX18.com|access-date=September 8, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170908212556/http://www.lex18.com/story/36322963/troy-gentry-of-montgomery-gentry-killed-in-helicopter-crash|archive-date=September 8, 2017|url-status=dead}}</ref> Through social media, the band released the following statement: \"It is with great sadness that we confirm that Troy Gentry, half of the popular country duo, Montgomery Gentry, was tragically killed in a helicopter crash which took place at approximately 1:00 p.m. today in Medford, New Jersey.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twitter.com/mgunderground/status/906245306777571328|title=Montgomery Gentry on Twitter|website=Twitter|publisher=Montgomery Gentry|access-date=September 9, 2017}}</ref> On September 14, 2017, a public memorial service for Gentry was held at the [[Grand Ole Opry]] in [[Nashville]].<ref name=funeral>{{Cite news |url=http://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/2017/09/11/troy-gentrys-funeral-arrangements-set/654559001/ |title=Troy Gentry funeral service at Grand Ole Opry in Nashville |first=Cindy |last= Watts |newspaper=[[The Tennessean]] |date=September 11, 2017}}</ref>  On November 5, 2018, the final [[National Transportation Safety Board]] report was issued, with the accident being primarily attributed to the pilot's ''\"failure to maintain [[Helicopter rotor|rotor]] rpm... which resulted in an uncontrolled descent.\"''<ref>{{cite news|url=https://app.ntsb.gov/pdfgenerator/ReportGeneratorFile.ashx?EventID=20170908X43517&AKey=1&RType=Final&IType=FA|title=NTSB Aviation Accident Final Report ERA17FA317|publisher=National Transportation Safety Board|access-date=November 28, 2018}}</ref>\n\n==Awards==\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Bailey_Zimmerman","to":"Bailey Zimmerman"}],"pages":{"70985374":{"pageid":70985374,"ns":0,"title":"Bailey Zimmerman","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=February 2024}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Bailey Zimmerman\n| image             = Bailey Zimmerman on YouTube.png\n| caption           = Zimmerman in 2023\n| alt               = A waist-up view of singer Bailey Zimmerman, holding a bottle in his left hand.\n| birth_name        = Bailey Lynn Zimmerman<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ascap.com/repertory#/ace/search/workID/912874870 |title=CHANGE |website=ASCAP |publisher=American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers |access-date=July 23, 2023}}</ref>\n| birth_date        = {{birth date and age|2000|01|27}}<ref>[https://www.countrythangdaily.com/bailey-zimmerman-facts/] Country Thang Daily</ref>\n| birth_place       = [[Louisville, Illinois]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{flatlist|\n* [[Country music|Country]]\n* [[Southern rock]]\n}}\n| occupation        = {{flatlist|\n* Singer\n* songwriter\n}}\n| instrument        = {{flatlist|\n*Vocals\n*guitar\n}}\n| years_active      = 2020\u2013present\n| label             = {{flatlist|\n* [[List of Warner Music Group labels#Warner Music Nashville|Warner Nashville]]\n* [[Elektra Records|Elektra]]\n}}\n| website           = {{URL|baileyzimmermanofficial.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Bailey Lynn Zimmerman''' (born January 27, 2000) is an American [[Country music|country]] singer. In 2022, he charted the singles \"[[Fall in Love (Bailey Zimmerman song)|Fall in Love]]\" and \"[[Rock and a Hard Place (Bailey Zimmerman song)|Rock and a Hard Place]]\", which both reached number one on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Country Airplay]] chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Asker |first=Jim |date=2023-05-01 |title=Bailey Zimmerman's 'Rock' Skips to Historic Sixth Week Atop Country Airplay Chart |url=https://www.billboard.com/pro/bailey-zimmerman-rock-and-a-hard-place-number-one-country-airplay-six-weeks/ |access-date=2024-04-11 |magazine=Billboard |language=en-US}}</ref> His debut album ''[[Religiously. The Album.]]'' was released on May 12, 2023. This album also includes the singles \"[[Religiously (song)|Religiously]]\" and \"[[Where It Ends]]\".\n\n==Early life==\nZimmerman was born in [[Louisville, Illinois]]. He began playing the guitar at the age of nine, devoting much of his childhood to riding dirt bikes and playing baseball.<ref>{{Cite web |last=@BCMF_Taylor |date=2024-02-19 |title=Get to Know Your BCMF 2024 Artists: Bailey Zimmerman |url=https://barefootcountrymusicfest.com/get-to-know-your-bcmf-2024-artists-bailey-zimmerman/ |access-date=2024-04-10 |website=Barefoot Country Music Fest |language=en}}</ref> His mother first introduced him to various [[hair metal]] bands as well as [[Kid Rock]], [[Avenged Sevenfold]], and [[Nickelback]] when he was a teenager.<ref name=\":0\" /> In 2012, his mother took him to his first concert, which was performed by [[Tesla (band)|Tesla]]. It was the only other concert he had attended before he became a singer.<ref name=\":0\"/> In comparison, his father would take long trips with Zimmerman playing [[country music]] on the radio.\n\nPrior to making music, he worked in the [[meat-packing industry]] in 2016. Shortly after graduating, he relocated to West Virginia to work on a union gas [[pipeline]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.warnermusicnashville.com/artist/bailey-zimmerman|title=Bailey Zimmerman (Bio)|work=[[Warner Music Group|Warner Music Nashville]]|access-date=June 19, 2022|archive-date=June 19, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220619014605/https://www.warnermusicnashville.com/artist/bailey-zimmerman|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=TikTok - Make Your Day |url=https://www.tiktok.com/@bailey.zimmerman/video/6877684211571117318 |access-date=2024-04-10 |website=www.tiktok.com}}</ref> He graduated from [[North Clay High School]] on May 12, 2018.<ref>{{Citation |title=2018 North Clay High School Graduation LIVE | date=May 12, 2018 |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JYGZrE8cJvQ |access-date=2024-02-21 |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |title=North Clay High School Alumni |url=https://www.allhighschools.com/school/north-clay-high-school/1000004743 |access-date=February 21, 2024 |website=AllHighSchools}}</ref> Due to a lack of time spent with his family, he quit pipelining to pursue a truck lift venture with his stepbrother's welding business Top Notch Metal Worx. He started promoting the business through his [[TikTok]] account to acquire customers.<ref>{{Cite AV media |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XGhkd-_nqic |title=How Bailey Zimmerman Accidentally Became A Country Star... |language=en |access-date=2024-05-10 |via=www.youtube.com}}</ref>\n\n== Career ==\n\n=== Early career (2020\u20132021) ===\nWhile awaiting the completion of a customer's build at his stepbrother's establishment, Bailey recorded himself singing \"[[Stay (Black Stone Cherry song)|Stay]]\" by [[Black Stone Cherry]] for [[Snapchat]]. His motivation was to impress girls. Songwriter Gavin Lucas, whose father had been Bailey's school bus driver in elementary school, came across Bailey's story and was taken aback by his singing ability. Lucas informed Bailey that the video had been widely shared, and he expressed interest in hearing some of Bailey's own songs.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Meet Bailey Zimmerman, Country's Biggest New Star Who Still Can't Believe He's Famous {{!}} GRAMMY.com |url=https://grammy.com/news/bailey-zimmerman-new-album-religiously-rock-and-a-hard-place-fall-in-love-tiktok-songs-never-comin-home-morgan-wallen-tour-opener-debut |access-date=2024-04-10 |website=grammy.com}}</ref> Several weeks later, while at his uncle's body shop, Lucas approached Bailey with a request to collaborate on a song. In response, Bailey penned the first verse of \"Never Comin' Home.\" Subsequently, they captured a video of Bailey performing the song with Lucas accompanying on guitar.<ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Freeman |first=Jon |date=2023-03-17 |title=Bailey Zimmerman Was Working a Gas Pipeline and Making Truck TikToks. Now He's Touring With Morgan Wallen |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/bailey-zimmerman-religiously-album-morgan-wallen-tour-1234698608/ |access-date=2024-04-10 |magazine=Rolling Stone |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nIn December 2020, Zimmerman started sharing original music on his TikTok account, notably featuring \"Never Comin' Home.\" Within a mere five hours, a snippet of the song had garnered over a million views. Motivated by this rapid success, he secured a studio in [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] to professionally record the track, investing $3,000. He made the decision to resign from his job shortly after. With finances tight, he turned to his mother, requesting $1,500. He conveyed to her the escalating traction of his song and his aspirations to pursue a career as a Country singer.<ref name=\":1\" />\n\nOn February 3, 2021, he released his debut single \"Never Comin' Home\", which later entered the top 20 on [[Spotify]]'s Viral Chart in the United States.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://charts.spotify.com/charts/view/viral-us-daily/2021-03-15/|title=Daily Viral Songs USA: March 15, 2021|work=[[Spotify]]|access-date=June 19, 2022}}</ref> The co-manager at 10th Street Entertainment Scott Frazier came across Zimmerman on TikTok and subsequently introduced him to Core Entertainment principals Kevin Zaruk and Simon Tikhman.<ref>{{Cite web |title=ZIMMERMAN UNBOUND |url=https://hitsdailydouble.com/music_city&id=327870&title=ZIMMERMAN-UNBOUND |access-date=2024-03-05 |website=HITS Daily Double |language=en}}</ref> He later signed to Core Entertainment in August 2021.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Hollabaugh |first=Lorie |date=2021-08-19 |title=Bailey Zimmerman Signs With The Core Entertainment, 10th Street Entertainment |url=https://musicrow.com/2021/08/bailey-zimmerman-signs-with-the-core-entertainment-10th-street-entertainment/ |access-date=2024-03-05 |website=MusicRow.com |language=en-US}}</ref> The same month, he performed his first show at \"Rock The South 2021\" with a backing band he only met three days prior to the performance.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Reynolds |first=Scott |date=2021-09-18 |title=Louisville artist manager helping musicians achieve dreams |url=https://www.wdrb.com/news/louisville-artist-manager-helping-musicians-achieve-dreams/article_f42d322e-18e5-11ec-bd4d-4f0574d5a041.html |access-date=2024-03-05 |website=WDRB |language=en}}</ref>\n\n=== Mainstream success (2022\u2013present) ===\nHis breakout single \"[[Fall in Love (Bailey Zimmerman song)|Fall in Love]]\" was released on February 11, 2022, and reached number 29 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] in October.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/hot-100/|title=Billboard Hot 100|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]}}</ref> This was followed by additional singles \"[[Rock and a Hard Place (Bailey Zimmerman song)|Rock and a Hard Place]]\" and \"Where It Ends\" in June and August 2022, respectively.<ref name=\"hard\"/> Due to the success of these songs, Zimmerman was signed to [[List of Warner Music Group labels#Warner Music Nashville|Warner Music Nashville]] and [[Elektra Records]],<ref>{{cite web | url=https://musicrow.com/2022/04/bailey-zimmerman-joins-warner-music-nashville-elektra-music-group-roster/ | title=Bailey Zimmerman Joins Warner Music Nashville, Elektra Music Group Roster | publisher=[[MusicRow]] | date=April 13, 2022 | accessdate=June 20, 2022}}</ref> with \"Fall in Love\" later charting at Country radio format.<ref name=\"hard\">{{cite web | url=https://tasteofcountry.com/bailey-zimmerman-rock-and-a-hard-place/ | title=Hear Bailey Zimmerman's Brooding New 'Rock and a Hard Place' | publisher=[[Taste of Country]] | date=June 14, 2022 | accessdate=June 20, 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://musicrow.com/2022/06/disclaimer-single-reviews-toby-keith-shows-off-his-mighty-vocals-on-oklahoma-breakdown/ | title=DISClaimer Single Reviews: Toby Keith Shows Off His Mighty Vocals On 'Oklahoma Breakdown' | publisher=MusicRow | date=June 16, 2022 | accessdate=June 20, 2022}}</ref>\n\nZimmerman released his debut major-label project ''[[Leave the Light On (EP)|Leave the Light On]]'' on October 14, 2022. It debuted in the top ten of the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] and [[Canadian Albums]] charts.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://etcanada.com/news/938822/bailey-zimmerman-shatters-country-records-with-debut-album/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221024230750/https://etcanada.com/news/938822/bailey-zimmerman-shatters-country-records-with-debut-album/|url-status=dead|archive-date=October 24, 2022|title=Bailey Zimmerman Shatters Country Records With Debut Album|date=October 24, 2022|first=Melissa|last=Romualdi|work=[[Entertainment Tonight Canada|ET Canada]]|access-date=November 2, 2022}}</ref> As a result of high demand, Zimmerman extended his headlining tour of the United States into the fall of 2022, with [[Josh Ross]] opening his early 2023 dates.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicmayhemmagazine.com/bailey-zimmerman-breaks-streaming-records-leave-the-light-on-becomes-the-biggest-streaming-country-debut-of-all-time/|title=Bailey Zimmerman Breaks Streaming Records & 'Leave The Light On' Becomes The Biggest Streaming Country Debut Of All Time|first=Ally|last=Roden|work=Music Mayhem Magazine|date=October 31, 2022}}</ref> He made his [[Grand Ole Opry]] debut on November 4, 2022.<ref>{{Cite web |title=BAILEY'S GRAND OLE DEBUT |url=https://hitsdailydouble.com/music_city&id=333630&title=BAILEY%E2%80%99S-GRAND-OLE-DEBUT |access-date=2024-03-05 |website=HITS Daily Double |language=en}}</ref> [[Morgan Wallen]] announced that Zimmerman would be one of the opening acts for his One Night at a Time World Tour in 2023.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2022-12-02 |title=MORGAN WALLEN ANNOUNCES 2023 ONE NIGHT AT A TIME WORLD TOUR - Side Stage Magazine |url=https://sidestagemagazine.com/morgan-wallen-announces-2023-one-night-at-a-time-world-tour/ |access-date=2024-03-05 |website=sidestagemagazine.com |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn March 17, 2023, Zimmerman announced his debut album ''[[Religiously. The Album.]]'', and it was released on May 12, 2023.<ref name=\"RTA RS\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/bailey-zimmerman-religiously-album-morgan-wallen-tour-1234698608/|title=Bailey Zimmerman Was Working a Gas Pipeline and Making Truck TikToks. Now He's Touring With Morgan Wallen|first=Joe|last=Freeman|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=March 17, 2023|access-date=March 17, 2023}}</ref> He will support the album with the \"Religiously: The Tour\" across the United States, Great Britain, and Ireland in 2024, with [[Josh Ross]] again joining him as an opening act.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://countrychord.com/bailey-zimmerman-announces-the-religiously-2024-tour/|title=Bailey Zimmerman Announces The \"Religiously\" 2024 Tour W/ Josh Ross|first=Clayton|last=Anderson|work=Country Chord|date=June 12, 2023|access-date=July 3, 2023}}</ref> \u201cRock And A Hard Place\u201d broke the record for the longest climb to the top 10 for a song by a soloist in ''Billboard'' Hot 100 history.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Black |first=Lauren Jo |date=2023-04-11 |title=Bailey Zimmerman Smashes Chart Records With Second No.1, 'Rock And A Hard Place' |url=https://countrynow.com/bailey-zimmerman-smashes-chart-records-with-second-no-1-rock-and-a-hard-place/ |access-date=2024-03-05 |website=Country Now |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn February 23, 2024, Zimmerman released \"[[Holy Smokes (Bailey Zimmerman song)|Holy Smokes]]\" as the lead single for his second album which was previously teased through TikTok.<ref>{{Cite web |last=White |first=Logan |date=2024-02-23 |title=Bailey Zimmerman shares new song \"Holy Smokes\" |url=https://substreammagazine.com/2024/02/bailey-zimmerman-shares-new-song-holy-smokes/ |access-date=2024-04-10 |website=Substream Magazine |language=en-US}}</ref> It debuted at No. 54. Zimmerman would be featured on the soundtrack for 2024 film <nowiki>''</nowiki>[[Twisters (film)|''Twisters''\"]] with his song \"Hell or High Water.\"<ref>{{Cite web |date=2024-05-24 |title=Bailey Zimmerman has his new song \"Hell or High Water\" in Twisters: The Album |url=https://www.rfdtv.com/bailey-zimmerman-has-his-new-song-hell-or-high-water-in-twisters-the-album |access-date=2024-06-18 |website=RFD-TV |language=en}}</ref> On June 17, 2024, Zimmerman created anticipation for his new track \"New To Country\" by teasing it on social media platforms, following its use as pre-concert hype music.<ref>{{Cite web |title=Bailey Zimmerman Offers Playful Response to Critics with Unreleased Song, 'New To Country' {{!}} Holler |url=https://holler.country/news/breaking/bailey-zimmerman-offers-playful-response-to-critics-with-unreleased-song-new-to-country |access-date=2024-06-18 |website=holler.country |language=en}}</ref>\n\n== Artistry ==\nZimmerman is noted for having a raspy, gritty voice with influences stemming from [[Nickelback]], Tesla, and [[Eric Church]].<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite web |last=Caramanica |first=Jon |date=2023-05-11 |title=How Bailey Zimmerman Charmed Nashville |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2023/05/11/arts/music/bailey-zimmerman-religiously-the-album.html |website=New York Times |id={{ProQuest|2811839088}}}}</ref> His sound is a mix of [[Rock music|rock]] and country.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2022-07-28 |title=7 Facts To Get To Know Bailey Zimmerman |url=https://warnermusic.co.nz/news/7-facts-to-get-to-know-bailey-zimmerman |access-date=2024-04-10 |website=[[Warner Music New Zealand]]}}</ref>\n\n== Personal life ==\n\nZimmerman is a Christian.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Chua |first=Jeremy |title=Faith inspires Bailey Zimmerman's new tattoo |url=https://southernillinoisnow.com/2023/07/31/faith-inspires-bailey-zimmermans-new-tattoo/ |access-date=2024-07-12 |website=South Central Illinois' News, Sports and Weather Station |language=en}}</ref> His parents divorced at the age of ten.<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite web |date=2023-10-12 |title=How Bailey Zimmerman's breakup songs made him country's breakout star |url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/music/story/2023-10-12/bailey-zimmerman-religiously-rock-and-a-hard-place |access-date=2024-04-10 |website=Los Angeles Times |language=en-US}}</ref> He has an older brother Dalton, and younger brother Nicholas.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.instagram.com/p/CuxlKrJoORd/?hl=en|title=Instagram|website=www.instagram.com}}</ref>\n\nOn February 11, 2023, Bailey performed at BetMGM\u2019s West [[Super Bowl]] Fest held at the [[Westgate Entertainment District]] in [[Glendale, Arizona]]. However, during his performance of \"Rock And A Hard Place,\" technical difficulties resulted in Bailey losing audio feedback, leading to an unintentional off-key performance. This incident garnered significant attention, with a TikTok video capturing the moment amassing over eleven million views.<ref>{{Cite web |title=TikTok - Make Your Day |url=https://www.tiktok.com/@tomatobisque22/video/7199149763294645550?lang=en |access-date=2024-05-10 |website=www.tiktok.com}}</ref> Consequently, Bailey faced accusations of being unable to sing. Responding to the ensuing backlash on February 15, Zimmerman, acknowledged the incident and issued a public apology.<ref>{{Cite web |last=MUSIC\u00b7 |first=Brady Cox\u00b7COUNTRY |date=2023-02-13 |title=Bailey Zimmerman Responds To Viral Super Bowl Weekend Performance: \"Ears Went Out\u2026 I Swear I'm Not THAT Bad\" |url=https://www.whiskeyriff.com/2023/02/13/bailey-zimmerman-responds-to-viral-super-bowl-weekend-performance-ears-went-out-i-swear-im-not-that-bad/ |access-date=2024-05-10 |website=Whiskey Riff |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n!
