This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Crossin_Dixon","to":"Crossin Dixon"}],"pages":{"14690080":{"pageid":14690080,"ns":0,"title":"Crossin Dixon","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country music and Southern rock band}}\n{{Single source|date=April 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Crossin Dixon\n| image           =\n| alias           = Kyote Wylde\n| origin          = [[Mississippi]], [[United States]]\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]], [[Southern rock]]\n| years_active    = 2002\u20132015\n| label           = [[Broken Bow Records|Broken Bow]]<br>[[Broken Bow Records|Stoney Creek]]\n| associated_acts = [[Jason Aldean]]<br />[[Paul Thorn]]<br />[[Jamie Davis (musician)|Jamie Davis and Soul Gravy]]\n| website         = http://www.crossin-dixon.com/\n| past_members    = Jason Miller<br />Michael Bole <br /> Brandon Hyde<br />Charlie Grantham\n}}\n\n'''Crossin Dixon''' is an American [[country music]] and [[Southern rock]] group signed to the independent [[Broken Bow Records|Stoney Creek Records]] label. It was founded by Jason Miller (vocals), Michael Bole, Brandon Hyde and Charlie Grantham.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web |url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p972084|pure_url=yes}} |title=allmusic ((( Crossin Dixon > Biography ))) |accessdate=2007-12-13 |last=Leahey |first=Andrew |work=[[Allmusic]]}}</ref> They have released three singles, of which two have charted on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' country charts.\n\n==Biography==\nThe four members of Crossin Dixon first performed together in 2002. Originally, they assumed the name Kyote Wylde, but after developing a significant fanbase, the band changed its name to Crossin Dixon in 2004, to reflect their widespread touring.<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> The band was recommended to record producer [[Michael Knox (record producer)|Michael Knox]], who had also worked with [[Jason Aldean]], and by 2006, Crossin Dixon was signed to [[Broken Bow Records]].<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> Their first single, entitled \"Guitar Slinger\", was released to radio in July 2007; both it and the followup, \"Make You Mine\", charted on the [[Hot Country Songs]] charts that year. They released a third single, \"I Love My Old Bird Dog (& I Love You Too)\" in 2008, but the single failed to chart.  Their self-titled debut was released digitally on December 16, 2008. They released a single called \"Lovin in the Country\" to radio and  on August 31, 2010, as the first single for an upcoming, untitled second album. A new single, \"Goodbye to Henry\", was released on December 6, 2010, but it failed to chart. \n\nCrossin Dixon took a brief hiatus in 2012 following the announcement of former singer, Jason Miller, to pursue a solo career. After careful thought and consideration for their fans, the two remaining members of Crossin Dixon, Brandon Hyde and Charlie Grantham, decided they would continue their tour starting in January 2013. The band broke up sometime in 2015, without making much noise or a formal announcement. \n\n==Discography==\n===''Crossin Dixon'' (2008)===\n{{Infobox album\n| italic_title = no\n| name       = ''Crossin Dixon''\n| type       = Studio\n| artist     = Crossin Dixon\n| cover      = CrossinDixon.jpg\n| alt        =\n| released   = November 18, 2008\n| recorded   =\n| venue      =\n| studio     =\n| genre      = Country\n| length     = 38:53\n| label      = [[Broken Bow Records|Broken Bow]]\n| producer   = [[Michael Knox (record producer)|Michael Knox]]\n| prev_title =\n| prev_year  =\n| next_title =\n| next_year  =\n}}\n;Track listing\n#\"Guitar Slinger\" ([[Rodney Clawson]], Jon Stone, [[Bob DiPiero]]) - 3:23\n#\"Don't Give Up on Me\" ([[Lee Brice]], Garrett Parris, [[Kyle Jacobs (musician)|Kyle Jacobs]]) -   3:37\n#\"Stomp\" (Clawson, Blair Daly, [[John Rich]]) - 3:07\n#\"Don't Waste Your Pretty\" ([[Willie Mack (musician)|Willie Mack]], Giles Godard) - 2:49\n#\"Let the Bad Times Roll\" ([[Brett James]], [[Hillary Lindsey]], [[Troy Verges]], Blair Daly) - 3:42\n#\"[[Nineteen (song)|Nineteen]]\" ([[Jeffrey Steele]], [[Gary Nicholson (singer)|Gary Nicholson]], [[Tom Hambridge]]) - 3:09\n#\"Make You Mine\" (Clawson, Stone) - 3:52\n#\"I Love My Old Bird Dog (& I Love You)\" (Bill Luther, James) - 4:09\n#\"I Can Try\" ([[Dave Berg (songwriter)|Dave Berg]], George Teren) - 3:06\n#\"Moonshine and Mountain Dew\" ([[Chris Tompkins]], [[Josh Kear]], [[Mark Irwin (songwriter)|Mark Irwin]]) - 3:13\n#\"Just Look What You've Done\" (James, [[John Bettis]]) - 4:46\n\n===Singles===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Johnny_Van_Zant","to":"Johnny Van Zant"}],"pages":{"1473365":{"pageid":1473365,"ns":0,"title":"Johnny Van Zant","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer (born 1960)}}\n{{BLP sources|date=December 2020}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Johnny Van Zant\n| image             = Johnny Van Zant (Lynyrd Skynyrd) (cropped).jpg\n| image_size        = \n| caption           = Van Zant in 2012\n| birth_name        = John Roy Van Zant\n| alias             = \n| birth_date        = {{Birth date and age|1960|2|27}}\n| birth_place       = [[Jacksonville, Florida]], U.S.\n| origin            = \n| genre             = [[Southern rock]], [[Country music|country]]\n| occupation        = Singer\n| years_active      = 1976\u2013present\n| label             = \n| current_member_of = [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]]\n| past_member_of    = [[Van Zant (band)|Van Zant]]\n}}\n\n'''John Roy Van Zant''' (born February 27, 1960), also known as '''Johnny Van Zant''', is an American singer and the current lead vocalist of [[Southern rock]] band [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]]. He is the younger brother of Lynyrd Skynyrd co-founder and former lead vocalist [[Ronnie Van Zant]], and of the [[38 Special (band)|38 Special]] founder [[Donnie Van Zant]].\n\n==Biography==\nDuring the 1970s, Van Zant performed with his first band, the Austin Nickels Band. They later changed their name to [[The Johnny Van Zant Band]] releasing their debut solo album, ''[[No More Dirty Deals]]'', in 1980. Early members of the Johnny Van Zant Band consisted of Van Zant on lead vocals, Robbie Gay on guitar, Danny Clausman, on bass, Erik Lundgren on lead guitar, Robbie Morris, drums and [[Joan Hecht]] (previously Joan Cusimano) and Nancy Henderson on background vocals. Van Zant released three more solo albums between 1981 and 1985, before taking a break from the music business.\n\nHe became lead vocalist and chief songwriter for the reunited Lynyrd Skynyrd in 1987 and continues to record and perform with them today. He released another solo album, ''Brickyard Road'', in 1990, which featured the popular title track, which was a #1 hit on the U.S. [[Mainstream Rock Tracks]] chart for three weeks. He also records and performs with his brother, Donnie, as [[Van Zant (band)|Van Zant]] since 1998. Van Zant and Lynyrd Skynyrd performed in Arizona on April 9, 2022, during Arizona Bike Week at WestWorld of Scottsdale. He stated that original member [[Gary Rossington]] was recovering and still needed prayers.\n\nIn May 2006, less than one day before he was to perform at [[KSAN (FM)|KSAN-FM]] 107.7 ''The Bone's Bone Bash 7'', Van Zant underwent emergency surgery to have his [[Vermiform appendix|appendix]] removed. Treated at [[Stanford University Medical Center]] in [[Palo Alto, California]], after reporting pain to a doctor earlier in the day. The incident forced the band to cancel three U.S. shows.<ref>[http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/entertainment/4997130.stm Notice of Johnny Van Zant surgery], bbc.co.uk; accessed August 11, 2015.</ref>\n\nVan Zant is a fan of the [[Jacksonville Jaguars]]. He recorded a video, along with remaining members of Lynyrd Skynyrd, that is played at every Jaguars home game on the [[TIAA Bank Field]] video board.<ref>{{Cite web |date=2018-08-31 |title=Jaguars and Skynyrd a Natural Fit |url=https://www.samsportsline.com/jaguars-and-skynyrd-a-natural-fit/ |access-date=2022-05-11 |website=Jacksonville Sports News, Sam Kouvaris SamSportsline.com |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nAccording to Skynyrd's website, Van Zant was again hospitalized on August 6, 2011, at the [[Hennepin County Medical Center]] in [[Minneapolis]], [[Minnesota]], due to complications from a previous surgery. According to the website, Van Zant had a \"surgical site\" infected with [[cellulitus]] which required both hospitalization and IV/Antibiotic treatment. He began displaying signs of a [[staphylococcal infection|staph infection]] and other symptoms related to the infection. His subsequent illness resulted in a number of scheduled performances being cancelled.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Newton|first=Steve|date=2011-08-11|title=Lynyrd Skynyrd's Johnny Van Zant hospitalized, numerous shows cancelled {{!}} Georgia Straight Vancouver's News & Entertainment Weekly|url=https://www.straight.com/blogra/lynyrd-skynyrds-johnny-van-zant-hospitalized-numerous-shows-cancelled|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160305005923/http://www.straight.com/blogra/lynyrd-skynyrds-johnny-van-zant-hospitalized-numerous-shows-cancelled|archive-date=2016-03-05|access-date=2022-02-06|website=[[The Georgia Straight]]|language=en}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n[[File:Johnny Van Zant.jpg|thumb|upright=1.2|Van Zant performing with Lynyrd Skynyrd in 2012]]\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n\n!Title !! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Blackberry_Smoke","to":"Blackberry Smoke"}],"pages":{"31954940":{"pageid":31954940,"ns":0,"title":"Blackberry Smoke","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American rock band}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=April 2022}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Blackberry Smoke\n| image             = Blackberry Smoke live in Oklahoma City on April 28, 2018.jpg\n| caption           = Blackberry Smoke performing in 2018\n| image_upright     = 1.2\n| origin            = [[Atlanta, Georgia]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{hlist|[[Southern rock]]|[[country rock]]|[[hard rock]]|[[blues rock]]|[[jam band]]}}\n| years_active      = 2000\u2013present\n| label             = [[BamaJam]], Southern Ground, [[Rounder Records|Rounder]], 3 Legged, [[Earache Records|Earache]] (Europe)\n| website           = {{URL|blackberrysmoke.com}}\n| current_members   = * Paul Jackson\n* Charlie Starr\n* Richard Turner\n* Brandon Still\n* Benji Shanks\n* Kent Aberle*\n* * Touring member since 2022\n| past_members      = * Brit Turner\n* Preston Holcomb\n}}\n\n'''Blackberry Smoke''' is an American country rock band formed in [[Atlanta]], [[Georgia (U.S. state)|Georgia]], in 2000. The lineup consists of Charlie Starr (lead vocals, guitar), Richard Turner (bass, backing vocals), Paul Jackson (guitar, backing vocals), and Brandon Still (keyboards).  Richard's brother Brit Turner was the band's drummer before his death in March 2024. In 2018, they added touring members Benji Shanks (guitar) and Preston Holcomb (percussion). They have released eight studio albums, two live albums and five extended plays.\n\n== History ==\nBlackberry Smoke was formed in Atlanta, Georgia, in 2000. They are the first independently released artist to hit No. 1 on the [[Billboard Country Albums|Billboard Country Album]] charts in modern history. Their debut album, ''Bad Luck Ain't No Crime'', was released in 2003. Their second album released in 2009, ''Little Piece of Dixie''. has been featured by ''[[Paste (magazine)|Paste]]'' magazine and other publications.<ref name=\"pastemag\">{{cite web |url=http://www.pastemagazine.com/blogs/whitman/2009/05/blackberry-smoke----little-piece-of-dixie.html |title=Blackberry Smoke \u2013 Little Piece of Dixie :: Blogs :: Andy Whitman on Music :: Paste |publisher=Pastemagazine.com |date=May 14, 2009 |access-date=January 9, 2013 |archive-date=March 5, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130305010734/http://www.pastemagazine.com/blogs/whitman/2009/05/blackberry-smoke----little-piece-of-dixie.html |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Phillips |first=Fred |url=http://somethingelsereviews.com/2012/08/12/blackberry-smoke-the-whippoorwill-2012/ |title=Blackberry Smoke \u2013 The Whippoorwill (2012) |date=August 12, 2012 |publisher=Somethingelsereviews.com |access-date=January 9, 2013}}</ref>\n\nIn 2015 Blackberry Smoke became the first small independent outfit to have an album, ''Holding All The Roses'', go to No. 1 on the Billboard Country Albums chart. This was the first time a non-mainstream-supported artist or band was able to achieve this feat in the modern era. Blackberry Smoke's 2016 album ''Like An Arrow'' did the same.<ref>{{cite web |url= https://www.savingcountrymusic.com/blackberry-smoke-goes-1-in-album-sales-with-you-hear-georgia/ |title=Blackberry Smoke Goes #1 in Album Sales with \"You Hear Georgia\" |work=Saving Country Music|date=June 7, 2021 }}</ref> They have performed throughout the United States, Europe, Australia, and South America. They have performed alongside numerous artists such as [[Tedeschi Trucks Band]], [[Guns n' Roses]], [[Zac Brown Band]], [[ZZ Top]], [[Eric Church]] and [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]].\n\n[[File:Blackberry Smoke in 2012.jpg|thumb|upright=1.1|Blackberry Smoke performing in 2012]]\nThe band had their first chart success with their third album, ''[[The Whippoorwill]]'', released in August 2012, reaching Top 40 on [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]].<ref>{{cite web |url= http://rockrevoltmagazine.com/blackberry-smoke-video-pictures/ |title=Watch Blackberry Smoke's new video & check out live pics! |work=Rock Revolt Magazine|date=January 18, 2013 }}</ref> The album was released under the Southern Ground record label.<ref name=\"sga-label\">{{cite web |url=http://www.southerngroundrecords.com/2011/05/12/zac-brown-launches-southern-ground-artists-label/ |title=Zac Brown Launches Southern Ground Artists Label \u00ab Southern Ground |publisher=Southerngroundrecords.com |date=May 12, 2011 |access-date=January 9, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120624075433/http://www.southerngroundrecords.com/2011/05/12/zac-brown-launches-southern-ground-artists-label/ |archive-date=June 24, 2012 |url-status=dead }}</ref> On August 26, 2012, they performed at a charity benefit called the Boot Ride with the cast of ''[[Sons of Anarchy]]'', partnered with The Boot Campaign at the Happy Ending Bar and Grill in [[Hollywood, Los Angeles|Hollywood]], [[California]].<ref name=\"boot-ride\">{{cite web |url=http://bootride.com/home.html |title=Boot Ride \u2014 Get Your Tickets NOW! |publisher=Bootride.com |access-date=January 9, 2013 |archive-date=August 17, 2012 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120817235718/http://www.bootride.com/home.html |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://somethingelsereviews.com/2012/08/12/blackberry-smoke-the-whippoorwill-2012/|title=Blackberry Smoke \u2013 The Whippoorwill (2012) \u2013 Something Else!|work=Something Else!|date=August 12, 2012|access-date=February 13, 2015}}</ref>\n\nOn November 12, 2014, they appeared among many others \u2013 [[Jamey Johnson]], [[Trace Adkins]], [[Warren Haynes]], [[Peter Frampton]], [[Gregg Allman]], etc. \u2013 in a show in tribute to Lynyrd Skynyrd at the Fox Theatre in Atlanta.\n\nThey moved to [[Rounder Records]] in 2014,<ref name=\"BS-Rounder-release\">{{cite web |url=http://www.blackberrysmoke.com/entry/blackberry-smoke-leave-zac-brown-s-label-ink-rounder-deal-for-new-album.html/ |title=Blackberry Smoke Leave Zac Brown's Label, Ink Rounder Deal for New Album |publisher=blackberrysmoke.com |date=November 6, 2014 |access-date=November 12, 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141112155510/http://www.blackberrysmoke.com/entry/blackberry-smoke-leave-zac-brown-s-label-ink-rounder-deal-for-new-album.html/ |archive-date=November 12, 2014 |url-status=dead }}</ref> and released ''[[Holding All the Roses]]'' produced by [[Brendan O'Brien (record producer)|Brendan O'Brien]] in early 2015.<ref>{{cite web |url= https://www.loudersound.com/reviews/blackberry-smoke-holding-all-the-roses-1 |title=Blackberry Smoke: Holding All The Roses |work=Louder Sound |first=Polly |last=Glass |date=January 23, 2015}}</ref> The album reached No. 1 on Billboard's Country Albums chart. The band spent much of the summer of 2016 on tour with [[Gov't Mule]].\n\nBlackberry Smoke released their fifth studio album, ''[[Like an Arrow]]'', featuring Gregg Allman, on October 14, 2016, via their own record label, 3 Legged Records.<ref>{{cite web|title=Album of the Month (October 2016): Blackberry Smoke, 'Like an Arrow' Read More: Album of the Month (October 2016): Blackberry Smoke, 'Like an Arrow' |url=http://theboot.com/blackberry-smoke-like-an-arrow-october-2016-album/|website=The Boot|date=October 3, 2016 |publisher=Taste of Country Network|access-date=October 27, 2016}}</ref> The album landed at No. 1 on the US ''[[Billboard charts|Billboard]]'' Country<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Top Country Albums|url=http://www.billboard.com/charts/country-albums|magazine=Billboard|publisher=Billboard|access-date=October 27, 2016}}</ref> and Americana/Folk<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Americana/Folk Albums|url=http://www.billboard.com/charts/americana-folk-albums|magazine=Billboard|publisher=Billboard|access-date=October 27, 2016}}</ref> charts as well as the UK Rock<ref>{{cite web|title=Official Rock & Metal Albums Charts|url=http://www.officialcharts.com/charts/rock-and-metal-albums-chart/|website=Official Charts|publisher=The Official UK Charts Company|access-date=October 27, 2016}}</ref> and Independent Albums<ref>{{cite web|title=Official Independent Albums Chart Top 50|url=http://www.officialcharts.com/charts/independent-albums-chart/|website=Official Charts|publisher=The Official UK Charts Company|access-date=October 27, 2016}}</ref> charts during release week. The band released its sixth studio album, ''Find A Light'', on December 19, 2018.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.blackberrysmoke.com/find-a-light|title=Blackberry Smoke \u2013 Find a Light|access-date=October 8, 2019|archive-date=October 8, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191008173715/https://www.blackberrysmoke.com/find-a-light|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\nIn 2019, the band released via [[Earache Records]] a live album and a film ''Homecoming: Live in Atlanta'', recorded at their annual Brothers And Sisters Holiday Homecoming event at the [[Tabernacle (concert hall)|Tabernacle]] in Atlanta in November 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.loudersound.com/news/blackberry-smoke-announce-homecoming-live-in-atlanta-live-album-and-film |title=Blackberry Smoke announce Homecoming: Live In Atlanta live album and film|first= Fraser |last=Lewry |date= September 9, 2019 |work=Louder Sound}}</ref> In 2021 the band released its seventh studio album, ''You Hear Georgia.''<ref>{{Cite web|last=Ehrenclou|first=Martine|date=February 24, 2021|title=Blackberry Smoke To Release New Album 'You Hear Georgia' Out May 28th, Share Title Track|url=https://www.rockandbluesmuse.com/2021/02/24/blackberry-smoke-to-release-new-album-you-hear-georgia-out-may-28th-share-title-track/|access-date=October 13, 2021|website=Rock and Blues Muse|language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn May 28, 2021, their album ''[[You Hear Georgia]]'' was released. It debuted at No. 1 on the Billboard Americana/Folk Chart.<ref>{{cite magazine|url= https://www.billboard.com/charts/americana-folk-albums/2021-06-12/ |title=Blackberry Smoke Americana/Folk Charts|date= June 12, 2021 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> It sold over 33k copies the first week, 12,239 copies in pure album sales. This was good enough to put it also at No. 1 in album sales in both country and rock, and No. 3 in all of music. The album also racked up another nearly 1 million streams its debut week. The album was produced by [[Dave Cobb]] and also features appearances by [[Jamey Johnson]] and [[Warren Haynes]].\n\nIn March 2024, the band announced drummer Brit Turner had died after a battle with [[glioblastoma]]. He was 57, and was diagnosed with the cancer in 2022.<ref>{{cite news |title=Blackberry Smoke Drummer Brit Turner Dies at 57 |url=https://therockrevival.com/rock-news/blackberry-smoke-drummer-brit-turner-dies-from-brain-cancer/ |access-date=4 March 2024 |publisher=The Rock Revival |date=4 March 2024}}</ref>\n\nOn April 5, 2024 Preston Holcomb announced via Facebook his last show would be April 27th and he would no longer be touring with the band. \n\n==Band members==\n'''Current members'''\n* Charlie Starr (Gray)<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.loudersound.com/features/southern-comfort-the-unconventional-story-of-blackberry-smoke|title=Southern comfort: the unconventional story of Blackberry Smoke|work=Louder|first=Polly|last=Glass|date=July 2, 2021|access-date=January 22, 2024}}</ref> \u2013 lead vocals, guitar (2000\u2013present)\n* Richard Turner \u2013 bass, backing vocals (2000\u2013present)\n* Paul Jackson \u2013 guitar, backing vocals (2000\u2013present)\n* Brandon Still \u2013 keyboards (2009\u2013present)\n\n* Benji Shanks \u2013 guitar, mandolin, dobro (2018\u2013present)\n\n'''Touring members'''\n\n* Kent Aberle \u2013 drums, percussion (2022\u2013present)\n\n'''Former members'''\n* Brit Turner- drums (2000\u20132024) (his death)\n* Preston Holcomb \u2013 percussion (2018\u20132024)\n\n== Discography ==\n\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|+List of studio albums, with selected peak chart positions and sales\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Randy_Owen","to":"Randy Owen"}],"pages":{"8938611":{"pageid":8938611,"ns":0,"title":"Randy Owen","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use American English|date=October 2023}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=October 2023}}\n{{short description|American country singer (born 1949)}}\n{{BLP sources|date=March 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Randy Owen\n| image               = Randy Owens cropped.jpg\n| caption             = Owen in 2013\n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = Randy Yeuell Owen\n| alias               = \n| birth_date          = {{birth date and age|1949|12|13}}\n| birth_place         = [[Fort Payne, Alabama]], U.S.\n| origin              =\n| instrument          = Vocals, guitar\n| genre               = [[Country music|Country]], [[southern rock]], [[bluegrass music|bluegrass]]\n| occupation          = Singer, songwriter\n| years_active        = 1969\u2013present\n| label               = [[RCA Records Nashville|RCA Nashville]] (in Alabama)<br />DMP/New Revolution (solo)<br />[[Broken Bow Records|Broken Bow]] (solo)\n| current_member_of = [[Alabama (band)|Alabama]]\n| website             = {{URL|randyowen.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Randy Yeuell Owen''' (born December 13, 1949) is an American [[country music|country]] musician. He is best known for his role as the lead singer of [[Alabama (American band)|Alabama]], a [[country rock]] band that saw tremendous mainstream success throughout the 1980s and 1990s. Alabama became the most successful band in country music, releasing over 20 gold and platinum records, dozens of number 1 singles, and selling over 75&nbsp;million records during their career. Owen also maintains a career as a solo performer. He released his solo debut ''[[One on One (Randy Owen album)|One on One]]'' in late 2008 and charted two singles from it.\n\nOwen was inducted into the [[Musicians Hall of Fame and Museum]] in 2019.\n\n== Biography ==\nRandy Yeuell Owen grew up on a farm near Fort Payne, Alabama. He is of [[English people|English]] and [[Scottish people|Scots]] ancestry. He dropped out of high school in the ninth grade, but he returned and graduated from Fort Payne High in 1969.\nIn the late 1960s, Owen and his cousin, Teddy Gentry, began playing music together. They recruited another cousin, Jeff Cook, to form a band, which they called Wildcountry. Their first public performance was at a high school talent show, which they won.\n\nOwen's music career was put on hiatus as he earned an English degree from [[Jacksonville State University]]. He was also a member of [[Pi Kappa Phi]], Delta Epsilon Chapter. Upon his graduation, however, the three cousins moved into an apartment in [[Anniston, Alabama]], and by 1973 were pursuing a full-time music career. In 1980, the band, now called [[Alabama (American band)|Alabama]], were signed to a recording contract by RCA Records and quickly reached country superstardom. For the next twenty-two years, Alabama had a tremendous impact on [[country music]], attracting a younger group of listeners, crossing over into pop radio, and paving the way for groups to be successful on country radio.\n\nAlabama released 21 gold, platinum, and multi-platinum albums, 42 singles that topped the charts at #1, and sold over 75 million records in total.  They have a star on the [[Hollywood Walk of Fame]] and were named the [[Academy of Country Music]]'s Artist of the Decade in 1989, and the [[Recording Industry Association of America]]'s Country Group of the Century in 1999.\n\nIn May 2002, the band announced their retirement during the [[Academy of Country Music]] Awards telecast.  For the rest of 2002 and 2003, they performed throughout the country in their American Farewell Tour.  In 2005, the band was inducted into the [[Country Music Hall of Fame]].\n\nOwen lives on his cattle ranch outside Fort Payne. He currently serves as an at-large member of the Board of Trustees of [[Jacksonville State University]]. In 2007, he was a judge on Season 5 of the country talent show ''[[Nashville Star]]''.\n\nOwen took over hosting duties for ''Country Gold'', the Saturday night [[classic country]] request program on [[Westwood One (1976\u20132011)|Westwood One]], beginning July 21, 2012. The show was reformatted upon Owen's arrival, switching to a pre-recorded format (the show's predecessor, ''Country Gold Saturday Night'', was originally live; requests are handled, as they had been with Owen's immediate predecessor, by an [[answering machine]]) [[voice-tracking|voicetracked]] from Owen's home, drifting to a more open-ended \"traditional country\" format (one that includes more 1990s songs and even some 2000s songs along with country-pop tunes more commonly associated with the [[classic hits]] format while moving away from the core songs of the classic country format) and shortening the show from five hours to four. (In protest of the change of format, previous ''Country Gold'' host Rowdy Yates relaunched his version of the show as \"The Original Country Gold\" through [[Compass Media Networks]] a year later.) Owen ended his run as host on April 2, 2016, with [[Terri Clark]] replacing him the following weekend.\n\n== Discography ==\n{{See also|Alabama discography}}\n\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Bo_Bice","to":"Bo Bice"}],"pages":{"1589371":{"pageid":1589371,"ns":0,"title":"Bo Bice","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American singer and musician}}\n{{Distinguish|Bo Bruce}}\n{{BLP sources| date=May 2011}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2023}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Bo Bice\n| image           = Bo Bice.jpg\n| caption         = Bo Bice in [[The American Idol Experience]] motorcade at [[Walt Disney World]].\n| birth_name      = Harold Elwin Bice Jr.\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|1975|11|1}}\n| birth_place     = [[Huntsville, Alabama]], U.S.\n| origin          = [[Helena, Alabama]], U.S.\n| website         = \n| occupation      = {{hlist|Singer|musician}}\n| years_active    = 1994\u2013present\n| instrument      = {{hlist|[[Acoustic guitar]]|[[electric guitar]]|[[lap steel guitar]]|[[mandolin]]|[[harmonica]]|[[piano]]|[[saxophone]]|[[Singing|vocals]]}}\n| genre           = {{hlist|[[Southern rock]]|[[hard rock]]|[[country rock]]}}\n| label           = {{hlist|[[RCA Records|RCA]]|Sugarmoney|Saguaro Road|[[Lofton Creek Records|Lofton Creek]]}}\n| past_member_of  = {{hlist|SugarMoney|[[Blood, Sweat & Tears]]}}\n}}\n\n'''Harold Elwin''' \"'''Bo'''\" '''Bice Jr.''' (born November 1, 1975) is an American singer and musician who was the runner-up against [[Carrie Underwood]] in the [[American Idol (season 4)|fourth season]] of ''[[American Idol]]''. Prior to auditioning for ''American Idol'', Bice released a solo album as well as a few albums with his bands while performing on the night club circuit.\n\nBice charted in 2005 at number two on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] with a rendition of \"[[Inside Your Heaven]]\" from ''American Idol''. He released the album ''[[The Real Thing (Bo Bice album)|The Real Thing]]'' after ''American Idol'' to minor success before being dropped by RCA Records. He started his own record label Sugar Money and subsequently released two more albums, ''[[See the Light (Bo Bice album)|See the Light]]'' and ''[[3 (Bo Bice album)|3]].'' He was also the lead singer of [[Blood, Sweat & Tears]] from 2013 until 2018.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.bloodsweatandtears.com/ |title=Blood Sweat & Tears official web site |access-date=2014-10-02 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006092029/http://www.bloodsweatandtears.com/ |archive-date=2014-10-06 |url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n== Childhood ==\nBice was born in [[Huntsville, Alabama]] to Nancy and Harold Elwin Bice. His mother was a gospel singer as were his grandmother, great-grandmother, and aunts. Bice was [[nickname]]d \"Bogart\" as a newborn by his grandmother, \"Granny Madge\", because she thought he had \"[[Humphrey Bogart]] eyes\". His family continued to call him Bogart, but when Bice was in kindergarten he shortened it to \"Bo\" because he did not think Bogart was cool. Bice's parents divorced when he was very young, and his mother remarried years later. Bice grew up with his mother and step-father, Earle Downes, a Coca-Cola manager, step-sisters Jenny and Sharan Downes, and half-brother John Cohran. Bice has two other half-siblings, Candace and Matthew, on his biological father's side. The Downes family moved around the [[Southern United States|South]] frequently. They lived in [[Georgia (U.S. state)|Georgia]], [[Alabama]], and [[Florida]], including the metro area of [[Atlanta]]. In 1990 when Bice was 14 years old they moved to England, as part of his step-father's European assignment with [[Coca-Cola]] in London.\n\nBice spent his teenage years living in [[Gerrards Cross]]. Bice attended [[London Central High School]], a [[United States Department of Defense|Department of Defense]] school primarily for children whose parents served in the military or worked at the U.S. Embassy. In high school, he carried his [[guitar]] everywhere and played [[American football|football]]. It was around this time when Bice worked with some English [[alternative rock]] musicians.{{citation needed|date=March 2013}} He formed his first band, Spinning Jenny, while living there. Bice would have graduated in 1994, but in the fall of 1993, Bice dropped out of high school just before turning 18 to move back to Alabama, where he earned his [[GED]] and attended classes at [[Calhoun Community College]] from November 1996 to May 1997.\n\n== Career==\n===Career beginnings and ''American Idol'': 1997\u20132005===\nUpon leaving Calhoun and spending one semester at the [[University of North Alabama]] in [[Florence, Alabama|Florence]], Bice turned professional and performed in shows all across the United States, the United Kingdom, [[Republic of Ireland|Ireland]], and Europe. He was a veteran of the [[nightclub]] circuit, releasing his first CD in 1995 with his band Purge.<ref>{{cite web |last=Ortega |first=Shawna |url=http://www.songfacts.com/int/2008/08/bo-bice.html |title=Bo Bice: Songwriter Interviews |publisher=Songfacts |date=2008-07-23 |access-date=October 5, 2008 |archive-date=October 18, 2009 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091018125127/http://www.songfacts.com/int/2008/08/bo-bice.html |url-status=dead }}</ref> His other pre-''Idol'' bands include Blue Suede Nickel and [[Sugar Money (band)|SugarMoney]]. Among his credits were opening for [[Blackfoot (band)|Blackfoot]] and [[Warrant (American band)|Warrant]] as well as performing live and recording with [[Johnny Neel]], formerly of [[The Allman Brothers Band]]. Bice had recorded other albums prior to his stint on ''American Idol'', which included ''Ex Gratia'' (1999) with his band Purge, and ''Recipe for Flavor'' (2000) with SugarMoney. In 2001, Bice was charged with purchasing [[cocaine]] at a [[strip club]]. In 2003, Bice was arrested for possession of [[Cannabis (drug)|marijuana]], [[drug paraphernalia]] and [[public intoxication]]. He avoided jail time by agreeing to enter a [[drug rehabilitation|drug program]].<ref>[https://archive.today/20120906201505/http://www.popcrunch.com/busted-100-celebrities-arrested-for-drug-possession/Busted! 100 Celebrities Arrested For Drug Possession] from PopCrunch.com</ref><ref>[http://www.thesmokinggun.com/archive/0427051_bo_bice_american_idol_1.html \"Idol\" Finalist Dodged Cocaine, Pot Raps] from ''[[The Smoking Gun]]''</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1500954/20050428/id_0.jhtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080502050128/http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1500954/20050428/id_0.jhtml |url-status=dead |archive-date=May 2, 2008 |title='Idol' Singer Bo Bice Has Drug Rap Sheet, Court Papers Show |publisher=MTV News}}</ref>\n\nFor the 2005 season, ''Idol'' producers raised their required age limit from 16\u201324 to 16\u201328. In August 2004, Bice\u2019s mother and several other family members encouraged him to go try out, since he was within the eligible age limit (he would turn 29 in November 2004). Along with [[Constantine Maroulis]] and [[Taylor Hicks]] (winner of Season 5), Bice was one of the oldest contestants to audition and participate on ''American Idol''. Bice and Maroulis were among the first contestants to compete using the [[Rock music|rock]] idiom.<ref name=\"Kaufman\">{{Cite web |last=Kaufman |first=Gil |title='American Idol' Vets Bo Bice, Constantine Maroulis Can't Stop Rockin' |url=http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1560421/20070524/bice__bo.jhtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070528063956/http://www.mtv.com/news/articles/1560421/20070524/bice__bo.jhtml |url-status=dead |archive-date=May 28, 2007 |access-date=2016-05-17 |publisher=MTV }}</ref> His performance in the audition stage of The Allman Brothers Band's song \"[[Whipping Post (song)|Whipping Post]]\" drew raves from the judges. His later performances established him as one of the favorites in the competition. During the final three performance show, Bice took the risk of performing without a band or backup singers. He sang \"In a Dream\", an obscure song recorded by [[Badlands (American band)|Badlands]].\n\nIn June 2005, Bice was quoted in ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' magazine that his last thought during the ''Idol'' finale was, \"Please, God, don't let me win this thing.\"<ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=2002&dat=20050616&id=7L8iAAAAIBAJ&sjid=E7YFAAAAIBAJ&pg=5114,4458921 |title=Bice: 'Please, God, Don't Let Me Win This Thing.' |work=Beaver County Times |date=2005-06-15 |via=Google News Archive Search}}</ref> In comments during a subsequent appearance on ''[[Today (NBC program)|The Today Show]]'', Bice backed off this stance a bit, saying that he thanked all those who had voted for him. He lost the final, ending up runner-up to [[Carrie Underwood]]. In Alabama, May 24 was declared \"Bo Bice Day\" by Governor [[Bob Riley (Alabama)|Bob Riley]]. Two members of the group [[Lynyrd Skynyrd]] surprised Bice during his trip home from ''Idol'' and performed \"[[Sweet Home Alabama]]\" with him in his home town of [[Helena, Alabama]].\n\n;Idol The single debuted at number two on the ''Billboard'' Hot 100 Chart and number one on the ''Billboard'' Hot Single Sales chart. Bice's single replaced [[Carrie Underwood]]'s version of the same song at number one. It was [[Gold certification|certified Gold]] in late July 2005. Bice was invited to the [[Bonnaroo Music Festival]] by [[Trey Anastasio]]. He sang a song with [[Willie Nelson]] at a Birmingham concert and was invited by Nelson to perform at [[Farm Aid]]. Bice appeared on [[Carlos Santana]]'s 2005 album ''[[All That I Am (Santana album)|All That I Am]]'' with the song \"Brown Skin Girl\". On June 15, 2005, Bice married long-time girlfriend Caroline Fisher in [[Helena, Alabama]]. Bice had met her when he was working as a guitar store manager, and frequented the Ragtime Cafe in [[Hoover, Alabama]] where she was working her way through college as a waitress. Their first child, a son, was born in September 2005.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.usatoday.com/life/people/2005-06-30-bice-marries_x.htm |work=USA Today |title='American Idol' runner-up Bo Bice marries |date=2005-06-30}}</ref> A second son was born in August 2008.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.usmagazine.com/american-idol-bo-bice-and-wife-welcome-baby-boy |title=EXCLUSIVE: American Idol Runner-Up Bo Bice & Wife Welcome Baby Boy |date=2008-08-05 |work=Us Magazine |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080903094459/http://www.usmagazine.com/american-idol-bo-bice-and-wife-welcome-baby-boy |archive-date=2008-09-03}}</ref> A third son was born in January 2010 this was Ean Bice.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://people.com/parents/bo-bice-welcomes-son-ean-jacob/amp/ |title=Bo Bice Welcomes Son Ean Jacob |date=2010-01-22 |work=People |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100130012523/http://celebrity-babies.com/2010/01/22/bo-bice-welcomes-son-ean-jacob/ |archive-date=2010-01-30 |access-date=2020-02-25}}</ref>  Their fourth child and first daughter was born in April 2012.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://tasteofcountry.com/bo-bice-baby-girl/ |title=Bo Bice Welcomes Baby Girl |date=24 April 2012 |work=Taste of Country}}</ref> They reside in [[Covington, Georgia]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://gocovington.com/Newsroom/newton-countys-newest-resident-bo-bice |title=Newton County's Newest Resident- Bo Bice |publisher=Covington-Newton County Chamber of Commerce |access-date=May 10, 2016 |archive-date=June 4, 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160604092628/http://gocovington.com/Newsroom/newton-countys-newest-resident-bo-bice |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\nOn July 31, 2005, Bice broke his foot while performing in concert in [[Manchester, New Hampshire]]<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.today.com/popculture/bo-bice-busts-his-foot-onstage-wbna8790926 |title=Bo Bice busts his foot onstage |work=TODAY.com|date=August 2005 }}</ref> but carried on with the tour. On August 18, Bice, who had been suffering from stomach pain for months, was rushed to the hospital for emergency intestinal surgery to remove a blockage caused by a life-threatening intestinal condition called [[intussusception (medical disorder)|intussusception]]. He was sidelined from the tour for several shows. During his absence from the tour, fellow contestants Anwar, Nikko, Scott, Anthony and Constantine paid tribute to Bice by singing \"[[Sweet Home Alabama (song)|Sweet Home Alabama]]\" and wearing Bo Bice T-shirts.<ref>[http://www.foxesonidol.com/cgi-bin/ae.pl?mode=1&article=article1763.art&page=1 foxes on idol] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20051016204318/http://www.foxesonidol.com/cgi-bin/ae.pl?mode=1&article=article1763.art&page=1 |date=October 16, 2005 }}</ref> Bice returned to the tour for the final two concerts in [[Syracuse, New York]], September 10 and September 11 (a [[benefit concert]] with proceeds going to the [[American Red Cross]] to help victims of [[Hurricane Katrina]]). In addition to playing that concert, he opened his home in Helena, Alabama to a family displaced by Hurricane Katrina.\n\nOn October 7, 2005, Bice introduced his own band, SugarMoney, in [[Mobile, Alabama]] at [[Bayfest (Mobile)|Bayfest]]. He performed two concerts the following week, including a benefit concert for the victims of Hurricane Katrina, but was back in the hospital the next day with surgery complications. In November Bice was named \"Heartland Hero of the Week\" on [[John Kasich]]'s show, ''[[Heartland with John Kasich|Heartland]]'', for giving up his house to the family displaced by Hurricane Katrina and for using his music to raise money for victims of Hurricane Katrina. [[Jim Croce]]'s family awarded Bice the \"Jim Croce 20th Annual Music Award\" because the Croce family had been greatly moved by Bice's performance of Croce's song \"Time in a Bottle\" while he was a contestant on ''American Idol''.\n\n===''The Real Thing'' and recurring medical problems: 2005\u20132006===\nBice's solo debut album, ''[[The Real Thing (Bo Bice album)|The Real Thing]]'', was released on December 13, 2005. It opened at number four. ''The Real Thing'' has the seventh-highest opening for a debut album by an ''American Idol'' finalist. Bice's band at the time appears with him on three tracks on ''The Real Thing'''s DualDisc version. In January 2006, [[Country Music Television|CMT]] aired an hour-long TV special\u2014called ''Bo Bice: In the Moment''\u2014which chronicled Bice's life post-Idol during the recording of his album, ''The Real Thing''. Their cameras had followed Bice around for months during the making of his album. The film showed both his joy with making an album and his frustration with recording other people's pop songs. The cameras also captured the birth of his son, Aidan. On December 18, Bice started [[coughing up blood]] while rehearsing for a performance on the 2005 [[Radio Music Awards]], and had to miss the show.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.upi.com/NewsTrack/Entertainment/2005/12/19/bo_bice_out_of_radio_music_awards/7382/ |title=Top News, Latest headlines, Latest News, World News & U.S News |work=United Press International |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090124151135/http://www.upi.com/NewsTrack/Entertainment/2005/12/19/bo_bice_out_of_radio_music_awards/7382/ |archive-date=2009-01-24}}</ref>\n\nIn February 2006, Bice kicked off a radio promo tour. During the ensuing year of promotional appearances and touring, Bice continued to suffer with the recurring intestinal condition which had not been repaired by the August 2005 surgery. In the span of just a few months during his various tours, Bice was hospitalized 20 times, checking out of the hospitals each time to honor his performance commitments. In March 2006, Bice sang on the ''American Idol'' Top 16 Results Show. In April 2006, Bice was one of the celebrity drivers featured in the [[Toyota Pro/Celebrity Race]] held in [[Long Beach, California]], that was sponsored by [[Toyota]] to benefit various children's hospitals of Southern California. On September 12, 2006, Bice released a cover of [[The Chambers Brothers]] 1968 smash hit, \"[[Time Has Come Today]]\", which was the theme song for a new [[Monopoly (game)|Monopoly]] commercial. In September 2006, Bice was a special guest star in a TV special called ''Decades Rock Live: Lynyrd Skynyrd & Friends''\u2014the friends being Bice, [[Hank Williams Jr.]], and [[3 Doors Down]].\n\nOn October 5, 2006, Bice underwent emergency surgery in [[Nashville, Tennessee]] to correct his recurring intestinal problem. The surgery came after several rounds of tests and doctors deemed his condition serious enough to operate immediately. The day after that surgery, a complication occurred and Bice had to undergo another surgery. During the subsequent recovery time, [[Ben Stiller]] invited Bice to record for the [[Will Ferrell]] film ''[[Blades of Glory]]'' produced by Stiller. Bice made several promotional appearances in connection with the releases. Bice was presented with a [[Music recording sales certification|gold record]] for ''The Real Thing'' not long after [[RCA]] dropped Bice from its roster.\n\n=== Sugar Money Records, ''See The Light'' and ''3'': 2007\u20132013 ===\nIn the spring and summer of 2006, Bice began to talk of his hopes for a second CD, saying that \"[he]'d like to go more rootsy, more country, more southern rock Bo.\"<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.semissourian.com/story/1167395.html |title=seMissourian.com: Entertainment: Banking on Bo (09/08/06) |work=seMissourian.com |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061017223120/http://www.semissourian.com/story/1167395.html |archive-date=2006-10-17}}</ref> Bice encouraged his fans to start a petition asking [[Clive Davis]] for Bo's original southern rock songs on a subsequent CD. The Grassroots Coalition to Hear More Bo started the online Petition to Hear More Bo, which collected over 5,300 signatures before it was closed February 21, 2007, after word broke that Bice was no longer with RCA. Bice subsequently formed his own record label called Sugar Money/StratArt (in partnership with [[Strategic Artist Management]]). He spent the next few months planning, writing, and recording music for his new album, ''[[See the Light (Bo Bice album)|See the Light]]''. Bice introduced many of his newly written songs on a short acoustic tour which began in May 2007 and ended a few weeks later with his hospitalization for flu and bronchitis. ''[[See the Light (Bo Bice album)|See the Light]]'' was released October 23, 2007.\n\n[[File:Bo Bice Share the Beat Atlanta 2008.jpg|thumb|right|upright|Bice in September 2008]]\nIn October 2007, Bice made an appearance on the TV show ''[[American Chopper|American Chopper: The Series]]'' in an episode which featured a custom-built Peavey Bike with a built-in guitar, microphone, and amp. [[Peavey Electronics|Peavey Electronics Corporation]] and Bice were working together to develop a Bo Bice guitar for their line of products. Bice had made appearances in Peavey Electronics Corporation's after school programs (in conjunction with National Afterschool Alliance) during which Peavey donated instruments to schools. In February 2008, Bice traveled to [[Kuwait]] and [[Afghanistan]] to perform for U.S. troops deployed in the region, and to thank them for their service. He went back to the war region in Fall 2008. During Spring and Summer 2008, Bice continued his tour promoting his ''See the Light'' album. He simultaneously spent a few weeks participating in a special tour called ''It Was Forty Years Ago Today'' with [[Todd Rundgren]], [[Denny Laine]], [[Lou Gramm]], and [[Christopher Cross]]. The tour paid tribute to the fortieth anniversary of the release of the [[Beatles]]' ''[[Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band|Sgt. Pepper\u2019s Lonely Hearts Club Band]]''.\n\nOn September 13, Bice participated in \"Share the Beat\", a benefit for the Georgia Transplant Foundation and the James Redford Institute for Transplant Awareness. Bice sang two tracks on the ''Brothers of the Southland'' CD,<ref>[http://www.southernfriedmagazine.com/magazine/modules.php?name=News&file=article&sid=185&mode=thread&order=0&thold=0 Southern Fried Magazine'' August 1, 2007]</ref> a compilation spearheaded by [[The Marshall Tucker Band]]'s [[George McCorkle]] who had died from cancer just days prior to the recording sessions. On December 2, Bice was invited to Washington to perform for President Bush. Throughout 2009, Bice continued touring to support ''See the Light''. Bice did tour dates with Lynyrd Skynyrd. Bice was honored with the prestigious Lifetime Presidential Volunteer Service Award for volunteering more than 4,000 hours of his time for worthy causes, such as [[Habitat for Humanity]], Katrina assistance, [[muscular dystrophy]], organ transplants, two concert tours for the military troops in Iraq, Kuwait, and Afghanistan, Safe House, and many others. In addition to the hours for which he received recognition, he has donated instruments, music equipment, meaningful personal memorabilia, and some of his own paintings to be auctioned off for charities.\n\nBice started 2010 with an acoustic tour to introduce some newly written songs that he was recording for his upcoming album.{{Citation needed|date=May 2011}} Bice's Sugar Money record label cooperated with [[Time Life]] for the album which was called ''3'', which was officially released on [[Saguaro Road Records]] on May 18, 2010.{{Citation needed|date=May 2011}} On October 12, 2010, Bice guest-starred on the syndicated game show ''[[Don't Forget the Lyrics!]]'' and won the $50,000 grand prize for his charity, [[MusiCares]]. Bice was the first celebrity contestant to win the grand prize by correctly singing the lyrics to all the songs in his round.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://blog.al.com/mcolurso/2010/10/taylor_hicks_bo_bice_on_dont_f.html |title=Bo Bice, Taylor Hicks to appear on 'Don't Forget the Lyrics' (with videos) |work=AL.com|date=October 12, 2010 }}</ref>\n\nIn 2013, Bice sang \"[[The Star-Spangled Banner]]\" at the [[NASCAR]] [[Feed the Children 300]] in [[Sparta, Kentucky]].{{Citation needed|date=July 2013}}\n\n== Discography ==\n\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Year\n! rowspan=\"2\"| Album details\n! colspan=\"3\"| Peak chart<br />positions\n! rowspan=\"2\"| [[Music recording sales certification|Certifications]]<br /><small>([[List of best selling music artists|sales threshold]])</small>\n|- style=\"font-size:smaller;\"\n! style=\"width:30px;\"| [[Billboard 200|US]]<br /><ref>{{cite magazine |url={{BillboardURLbyName |artist=bo bice |chart=Billboard 200}}|title=Bo Bice Album & Song Chart History: Billboard 200|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2010-08-01}}</ref>\n! style=\"width:30px;\"| [[Independent Albums|US Indie]]<br /><ref>{{cite magazine |url={{BillboardURLbyName |artist=bo bice |chart=Independent Albums}}|title=Bo Bice Album & Song Chart History: Independent Albums|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2010-08-01}}</ref>\n! style=\"width:30px;\"| [[Canadian Albums Chart|CAN]]<br /><ref>{{cite web |url=http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Charts/ALBUMS.html |archive-url=https://archive.today/20041226005640/http://jam.canoe.ca/Music/Charts/ALBUMS.html |archive-date=2004-12-26 |url-status=usurped |title=CANOE -- JAM! ''Decatur Daily''.\n\n{{Blood, Sweat & Tears}}\n{{American Idol 4}}\n{{American Idol}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Bice, Bo}}\n[[Category:1975 births]]\n[[Category:American Idol participants]]\n[[Category:American male pop singers]]\n[[Category:American pop rock singers]]\n[[Category:American harmonica players]]\n[[Category:American country rock singers]]\n[[Category:Idols (franchise) participants]]\n[[Category:Musicians from Huntsville, Alabama]]\n[[Category:Musicians from Birmingham, Alabama]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:University of North Alabama people]]\n[[Category:Lofton Creek Records artists]]\n[[Category:19 Recordings artists]]\n[[Category:People from Helena, Alabama]]\n[[Category:Country musicians from Alabama]]\n[[Category:Calhoun Community College alumni]]\n[[Category:21st-century American male singers]]\n[[Category:21st-century American singers]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"The_Wild_Feathers","to":"The Wild Feathers"}],"pages":{"49184885":{"pageid":49184885,"ns":0,"title":"The Wild Feathers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = The Wild Feathers\n| image           = The Wild Feathers 9 07 2013 (9700799181).jpg\n| image_size      =\n| origin          = [[Nashville]], [[Tennessee]], United States\n| genre           = [[Country music|Country]], [[Southern rock]], [[Rock music|rock]], [[heartland rock]], [[alternative rock]]\n| years_active    = 2010\u2013present<ref>{{cite web|author=James Christopher Monger |url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/the-wild-feathers-mw0002543593 |title=The Wild Feathers - The Wild Feathers &#124; Songs, Reviews, Credits |publisher=[[AllMusic]] |date=2013-08-13 |accessdate=2016-05-13}}</ref>\n| label           = [[Independent record label|Independent]]\n| website         = http://thewildfeathers.com\n| current_members = Joel King<br />Ricky Young<br />Taylor Burns<br />Ben Dumas<br />Brett Moore\n| past_members    = [[Preston Wimberly]] (guitar) and Aaron Spraggs (drums) Daniel Donato (guitar)\n}}\n\n'''The Wild Feathers''' are an American country rock band formed in 2010 in [[Nashville]], [[Tennessee]], United States, by Ricky Young, Joel King, and Taylor Burns, all of whom were lead singers in previous bands. Drummer Ben Dumas joined the band following the release of their debut album in the Summer of 2013.<ref>{{cite web|author=Ed Grisamore |url=https://www.macon.com/news/local/news-columns-blogs/ed-grisamore/article215246170.html|title=Losing a coin flip led this drummer to a life-long passion and career |publisher=[[Macon Telegraph]] |date=2018-07-22 |accessdate=2020-02-05}}</ref> Multi-instrumentalist Brett Moore (formerly a member of [[The Apache Relay|Apache Relay]], a band that had opened for The Wild Feathers) began touring with the band in 2015 and recording with the band for 2018's \"Greetings From The Neon Frontier\" album. The band's second studio album, ''Lonely Is a Lifetime'', was released March 11, 2016.<ref>{{cite web|author=James Christopher Monger |url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/the-wild-feathers-mn0003101327/biography |title=The Wild Feathers &#124; Biography & History |publisher=[[AllMusic]] |date= |accessdate=2016-05-13}}</ref> Their third studio album titled \"Greetings from the Neon Frontier\" was released June 29, 2018.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/rock/8463071/the-wild-feathers-wildfire-making-of|title=The Wild Feathers Talk Making of 'Wildfire': 'It's Almost a Love Letter to the Band'|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2018-06-28}}</ref>\n\n== History ==\nThe Wild Feathers was formed in 2010 by artists Joel King, Ricky Young, Taylor Burns, and [[Preston Wimberly]].<ref name=\"Reichard\">{{Cite web|url=https://madison.com/daily-cardinal/ricky-young-of-the-wild-feathers-talks-about-beginnings-and/article_f6969aa6-961f-11e3-96ce-0019bb2963f4.html|title=Ricky Young of The Wild Feathers talks about beginnings and The Band|last=Reichard|first=Sean|website=madison.com|date=15 February 2014 |language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> Burns and Wimberly were high school friends, and had previously played together in a band called Noble Dog.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.dallasobserver.com/music/the-wild-feathers-grew-up-on-dallas-blues-7051068|title=The Wild Feathers Grew Up on Dallas Blues|last=Dearmore|first=Kelly|date=2014-01-24|website=Dallas Observer|access-date=2020-01-01}}</ref> The band's four original members all contributed both vocals and guitar to the band.<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite web|url=https://relix.com/articles/detail/the_wild_feathers_deja_vu_all_over_again/|title=The Wild Feathers: D\u00e9j\u00e0 Vu All Over Again|date=2016-05-09|website=Relix Media|language=en-US|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> The band was signed by Jeff Sosnow, an [[A&r|A&R]] man at [[Interscope Records]] before playing a single live session or recording any songs. They were dropped by Interscope Records before finishing their first album and signed to [[Warner Records]], where Sosnow had begun working.<ref name=\":0\" />\n\nThe Wild Feathers began touring in 2013, playing hundreds of show with acts like [[Bob Dylan]], [[Willie Nelson]], and [[ZZ Ward]],<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.guitarworld.com/acoustic-nation/acoustic-nation-wild-feathers-jimmy-kimmel-live-tonight-and-rachael-ray-performance-confirmed-december-10th|title=The Wild Feathers on 'Jimmy Kimmel Live' Tonight and 'Rachael Ray' Performance Confirmed for December 10th|last=Nation 2013-12-02T21:36:44Z|first=Acoustic|website=guitarworld|date=2 December 2013 |language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> and playing at venues like [[Hangout Music Festival]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.al.com/entertainment/2014/05/things_started_coming_together.html|title=Things Started Coming Together for The Wild Feathers at the 2013 Hangout Festival|last=Oldshue|first=Lynn|date=2014-05-13|website=al|language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> Their self titled album, produced by [[Jay Joyce]], was released in the summer of 2013 and charted at #1 on the Billboard Heatseeker's Chart and at #109 on the ''[[Billboard 200]]'', resulting in invites to appear on various television programs, as well as acclaim from major music publications.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://countryfancast.com/country-music-bands-the-wild-feathers/|title=Country Music: Meet The Wild Feathers Band|last=steve|website=countryfancast.com|date=31 May 2018 |language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> Their single \"The Ceiling\" peaked at #7 on [[Adult Alternative Songs]] in October 2013.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://outandaboutnashville.com/february-the-month-in-music/|title=February: the Month in Music|last=Brant|first=Joseph|date=2016-02-29|website=Out & About Nashville - LGBT news, events and gay guide|language=en-US|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> Guitarist and vocalist Preston Wimberly left the band in late 2015.\n\nWhile on tour, the band began working on their second album, ''Lonely Is A Lifetime'', which was released on March 11, 2016.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/music/2016/03/25/wild-feathers-soar-70s-style-harmonies/82231774/|title=Wild Feathers soar with '70s-style harmonies|last=Lenahan|first=Jim|website=USA TODAY|language=en-US|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> On June 25, 2016 The Wild Feathers recorded ''Live At The Ryman'', played to a soldout [[Ryman Auditorium]]. ''Live At The Ryman'' celebrated the band's return to Nashville and the release of ''Lonely Is A Lifetime''. Former-member Preston Wimberly made a guest appearance on the track \"Left My Woman\", from ''Live At The Ryman''.<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/hear-the-wild-feathers-earnest-left-my-woman-at-the-ryman-105489/|title=Hear the Wild Feathers' Earnest 'Left My Woman' at the Ryman|last=Crawford|first=Robert|date=2016-12-01|magazine=Rolling Stone|language=en-US|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref>\n\nOn June 29, 2018 The Wild Feathers released their third album ''Greetings from the Neon Frontier'', which was produced with [[Jay Joyce]]<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://roughstock.com/news/2018/07/43168-album-review-the-wild-feathers-greetings-from-the-neon-frontier|title=Album Review: The Wild Feathers - \"Greetings From The Neon Frontier\"|date=2018-07-05|website=RoughStock|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref>\n\nOn November 20, 2020, the band independently released ''Medium Rarities'', an album featuring 11 previously unreleased songs from the band's 10-year career.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Fox |first1=Randy |title=The Wild Feathers Satisfy Old Tastes and New Cravings with Medium Rarities |url=https://www.theeastnashvillian.com/the-wild-feathers-satisfy-old-tastes-and-new-cravings-with-medium-rarities/ |website=The East Nashvillian |date=3 December 2020 |access-date=17 May 2021}}</ref> The album includes covers of \u201cBlue\u201d by [[The Jayhawks]], \u201c[[Almost Cut My Hair]],\u201d by [[Crosby, Stills, Nash & Young]], and \u201c[[The Guitar Man]]\u201d by [[Bread (band)]].\n\n== Style and influences ==\nThe Wild Feathers features the harmonic talents of multiple vocalists, including King, Young, and Burns.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://lifeminute.tv/music/video/wild-feathers-bring-back-good-old-rock-roll|title=The Wild Feathers Bring Back 'Good Old Rock & Roll'|website=lifeminute.tv|language=en|access-date=2019-12-31}}</ref> The Wild Feathers have been noted for their blend of [[Southern rock]] and [[Americana (music)|Americana]],<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.musictimes.com/articles/910/20130815/wild-feathers-album-review-nashville-band-break-past-americana-ceiling.htm|title=The Wild Feathers 'The Wild Feathers' Album Review: Can Nashville Band Break Past the Americana 'Ceiling' of Contemporaries Dawes, Houndmouth? [VIDEO]|date=2013-08-15|website=Music Times|language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> [[blues]],<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nashvillescene.com/music/article/13064597/the-wild-feathers-raise-the-ceiling-at-soldout-ryman-debut|title=The Wild Feathers Raise the Ceiling at Sold-Out Ryman Debut|website=Nashville Scene|date=27 June 2016 |language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref> and [[folk music]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.wfuv.org/content/wfuv-sxsw-wild-feathers-hotel-san-jose|title=WFUV at SXSW: The Wild Feathers at Hotel San Jose {{!}} WFUV|website=www.wfuv.org|access-date=2019-12-31}}</ref> Ricky Young acknowledged the influence of [[The Band]] on the group's sound, but pointed out that there were many other inspirations behind The Wild Feather's sound.<ref name=\"Reichard\"/> The Wild Feathers have cited acts like [[Tom Petty]], [[The Eagles (UK band)|The Eagles]], and [[Otis Redding]] as inspirations.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://theboot.com/the-wild-feathers-country-music-bio-facts/|title=Who Are the Wild Feathers? 5 Things You Need to Know|last=Liptak|first=Carena|website=The Boot|date=30 April 2018 |language=en|access-date=2019-12-30}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{|class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:33px;\"| Year\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:215px;\"| Album details\n!colspan=\"5\"| Peak chart positions\n|-\n!style=\"width:2em;font-size:75%\"| [[Billboard 200|US 200]]\n!style=\"width:2em;font-size:75%\"| [[Top Heatseekers|US Heat]]\n!style=\"width:2em;font-size:75%\"| [[Billboard charts#Albums|US Alt]]\n!style=\"width:2em;font-size:75%\"| [[Billboard charts#Albums|US Rock]]\n!style=\"width:2em;font-size:75%\"| [[UK Albums Chart|UK]]\n|-\n| style=\"text-align:center;\"| 2013\n|'''''The Wild Feathers'''''\n*Label: [[Warner Bros.
